(Indic)">rendering support</a> to display the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_language" title="Khmer language">Khmer</a> text in this article correctly.</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Cambodia</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">k</span><span title="/&#230;/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">&#230;</span><span title="\'m\' in \'my\'">m</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="\'b\' in \'buy\'">b</span><span title="/o&#650;/: \'o\' in \'code\'">o&#650;</span><span title="\'d\' in \'dye\'">d</span><span title="/i/: \'y\' in \'happy\'">i</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Cambodia.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" decoding="async" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a></span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e4/En-us-Cambodia.ogg" title="En-us-Cambodia.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-7">[7]</a></sup> also <b>Kampuchea</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/&#716;/: secondary stress follows">&#716;</span><span title="\'k\' in \'kind\'">k</span><span title="/&#230;/: \'a\' in \'bad\'">&#230;</span><span title="\'m\' in \'my\'">m</span><span title="\'p\' in \'pie\'">p</span><span title="/&#650;/: \'u\' in \'push\'">&#650;</span><span title="/&#712;/: primary stress follows">&#712;</span><span title="/t&#643;/: \'ch\' in \'China\'">t&#643;</span><span title="/i&#720;/: \'ee\' in \'fleece\'">i&#720;</span><span title="/&#601;/: \'a\' in \'about\'">&#601;</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Khmer_language" title="Khmer language">Khmer</a>: <span lang="km">&#6016;&#6040;&#6098;&#6038;&#6075;&#6023;&#6070;</span> <small>Khmer: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Khmer" title="Help:IPA/Khmer">[kam.pu.ci&#601;]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Cambodge</i>), officially the <b>Kingdom of Cambodia</b> (<a href="/wiki/Khmer_language" title="Khmer language">Khmer</a>: <span lang="km">&#6038;&#6098;&#6042;&#6087;&#6042;&#6070;&#6023;&#6070;&#6030;&#6070;&#6021;&#6016;&#6098;&#6042;&#6016;&#6040;&#6098;&#6038;&#6075;&#6023;&#6070;</span>, <i lang="km-Latn" title="Khmer language text">pr&#277;&#601;h ri&#601;ci&#601;naacak kampuci&#601;</i>, <small>IPA: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Khmer" title="Help:IPA/Khmer">[pr&#277;&#601;h ri&#601;.ci&#601;.na&#720;.ca&#660; kam.pu.ci&#601;]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Royaume du Cambodge</i>), is a country located in the southern portion of the <a href="/wiki/Indochina" title="Indochina">Indochina</a> peninsula in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>. It is 181,035 square kilometres (69,898 <a href="/wiki/Square_mile" title="Square mile">square miles</a>) in area, bordered by <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> to the northwest, <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a> to the northeast, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> to the east and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Thailand" title="Gulf of Thailand">Gulf of Thailand</a> to the southwest. The <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a>  of Cambodia has a population of over 16 million. The official religion is <a href="/wiki/Theravada" title="Theravada">Theravada</a> <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a>, practised by approximately 95 percent of the population. The country\'s minority groups include <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_people" title="Vietnamese people">Vietnamese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Han_Chinese" title="Han Chinese">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chams" title="Chams">Chams</a> and 30 <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Loeu" title="Khmer Loeu">hill tribes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The capital and largest city is <a href="/wiki/Phnom_Penh" title="Phnom Penh">Phnom Penh</a>, the political, economic and cultural centre of Cambodia. The kingdom is an <a href="/wiki/Elective_monarchy" title="Elective monarchy">elective</a> <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Cambodia" title="Monarchy of Cambodia">monarch</a>, currently <a href="/wiki/Norodom_Sihamoni" title="Norodom Sihamoni">Norodom Sihamoni</a>, chosen by the <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Cambodia" title="Politics of Cambodia">Royal Throne Council</a> as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Cambodia" title="Prime Minister of Cambodia">Prime Minister</a>, currently <a href="/wiki/Hun_Sen" title="Hun Sen">Hun Sen</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_current_longest_ruling_non-royal_leaders" title="List of current longest ruling non-royal leaders">longest serving non-royal leader</a> in Southeast Asia, ruling Cambodia since 1985.\nIn 802 AD, <a href="/wiki/Jayavarman_II" title="Jayavarman II">Jayavarman II</a> declared himself king, uniting the warring Khmer princes of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chenla_Kingdom" title="Chenla Kingdom">Chenla</a> under the name "Kambuja".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CHANDLER_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-CHANDLER-9">[9]</a></sup> This marked the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Empire" title="Khmer Empire">Khmer Empire</a>, which flourished for over 600 years, allowing successive kings to control and exert influence over much of Southeast Asia and accumulate immense power and wealth. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indianised_kingdom" title="Indianised kingdom">Indianised kingdom</a> facilitated the spread of first <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> and then <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> to much of Southeast Asia and undertook many religious infrastructural projects throughout the region, including the construction of more than 1,000 temples and monuments in <a href="/wiki/Angkor" title="Angkor">Angkor</a> alone. <a href="/wiki/Angkor_Wat" title="Angkor Wat">Angkor Wat</a> is the most famous of these structures and is designated as a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>. After the fall of Angkor to <a href="/wiki/Ayutthaya_Kingdom" title="Ayutthaya Kingdom">Ayutthaya</a> in the 15th century, a reduced and weakened Cambodia was then ruled as a <a href="/wiki/Vassal_state" title="Vassal state">vassal state</a> by its neighbours. In 1863, Cambodia became a <a href="/wiki/French_Protectorate_of_Cambodia" title="French Protectorate of Cambodia">protectorate of France</a>, which doubled the size of the country by reclaiming the north and west from Thailand.\n</p><p>Cambodia gained independence in 1953. The <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> extended into the country with the US bombing of Cambodia from <a href="/wiki/Operation_Menu" title="Operation Menu">1969</a> until <a href="/wiki/Operation_Freedom_Deal" title="Operation Freedom Deal">1973</a>. Following the <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_coup_of_1970" title="Cambodian coup of 1970">Cambodian coup of 1970</a> which installed the right-wing pro-US <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Republic" title="Khmer Republic">Khmer Republic</a>, the deposed king gave his support to his former enemies, the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a>. The Khmer Rouge emerged as a major power, taking Phnom Penh in 1975 and later carrying out the <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_genocide" title="Cambodian genocide">Cambodian genocide</a> from 1975 until 1979, when they were ousted by Vietnam and the Vietnamese-backed <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Kampuchea" title="People\'s Republic of Kampuchea">People\'s Republic of Kampuchea</a>, supported by the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Cambodian%E2%80%93Vietnamese_War" title="Cambodian&#8211;Vietnamese War">Cambodian&#8211;Vietnamese War</a> (1979&#8211;91). Following the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1991_Paris_Peace_Accords" title="1991 Paris Peace Accords">1991 Paris Peace Accords</a>, Cambodia was governed briefly by a <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Transitional_Authority_in_Cambodia" title="United Nations Transitional Authority in Cambodia">United Nations mission</a> (1992&#8211;93). The UN withdrew after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cambodian_general_election,_1993" title="Cambodian general election, 1993">holding elections</a> in which around 90 percent of the registered voters cast ballots. The <a href="/wiki/1997_clashes_in_Cambodia" title="1997 clashes in Cambodia">1997 factional fighting</a> resulted in the ousting of the government by Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Hun_Sen" title="Hun Sen">Hun Sen</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_People%27s_Party" title="Cambodian People\'s Party">Cambodian People\'s Party</a>, who remain in power as of  2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cambodia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>.\n</p><p>Cambodia is a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> since 1955, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a>, the <a href="/wiki/East_Asia_Summit" title="East Asia Summit">East Asia Summit</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WTO" title="WTO">WTO</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Non-Aligned Movement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">La Francophonie</a>. According to several foreign organisations, the country has widespread poverty,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> pervasive corruption,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> lack of political freedoms,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> low human development<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNDP_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNDP-13">[13]</a></sup> and a high rate of hunger.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Cambodia has been described by <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>\'s Southeast Asian Director, David Roberts, as a "vaguely communist free-market state with a relatively authoritarian coalition ruling over a superficial democracy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-17">[17]</a></sup> While per capita income remains low compared to most neighbouring countries, Cambodia has one of the fastest growing economies in Asia, with growth averaging 7.6 percent over the last decade. Agriculture remains the dominant economic sector, with strong growth in textiles, construction, garments and tourism leading to increased foreign investment and international trade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> The US <a href="/wiki/World_Justice_Project" title="World Justice Project">World Justice Project</a>\'s 2015 Rule of Law Index ranked Cambodia 76 out of 102 countries, similar to other countries in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PPPWJP_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-PPPWJP-19">[19]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">Citations</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-50"><a href="#Cited_sources"><span class="tocnumber">10.2</span> <span class="toctext">Cited sources</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-51"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name"><span id="Name"></span> Name</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Names_of_Cambodia" title="Names of Cambodia">Names of Cambodia</a></div>\n<p>The "Kingdom of Cambodia" is the official English name of the country. The English "Cambodia" is an anglicisation of the French "Cambodge", which in turn is the French transliteration of the Khmer <span lang="km" title="Khmer language text">&#6016;&#6040;&#6098;&#6038;&#6075;&#6023;&#6070;</span> <i>kampuci&#601;</i>. <i>Kampuchea</i> is the shortened alternative to the country\'s official name in Khmer <span lang="km" title="Khmer language text">&#6038;&#6098;&#6042;&#6087;&#6042;&#6070;&#6023;&#6070;&#6030;&#6070;&#6021;&#6016;&#6098;&#6042;&#6016;&#6040;&#6098;&#6038;&#6075;&#6023;&#6070;</span> <i>pr&#277;&#601;h ri&#601;ci&#601;naacak kampuci&#601;</i>. The Khmer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endonym" title="Endonym">endonym</a> <i>Kampuchea</i> derives from the Sanskrit name <span lang="sa" title="Sanskrit language text">&#2325;&#2350;&#2381;&#2348;&#2379;&#2332;&#2342;&#2375;&#2358;</span> <i>kambojade&#347;a</i>, composed of <span lang="sa" title="Sanskrit language text">&#2342;&#2375;&#2358;</span> <i>de&#347;a</i> ("land of" or "country of") and <span lang="sa" title="Sanskrit language text">&#2325;&#2350;&#2381;&#2348;&#2379;&#2332;</span> <i>kamboja</i>, which alludes to the foundation myths of the first ancient Khmer kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The term <i>Cambodia</i> was already in use in Europe as early as 1524, since <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Pigafetta" title="Antonio Pigafetta">Antonio Pigafetta</a> (an Italian explorer who followed <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">Ferdinand Magellan</a> in his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Circumnavigation_of_the_globe" title="Circumnavigation of the globe">circumnavigation of the globe</a>) cites it in his work <i>Relazione del primo viaggio intorno al mondo</i> (1524-1525) as <i>Camogia</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Colloquially, Cambodians refer to their country as either <span lang="km" title="Khmer language text">&#6047;&#6098;&#6042;&#6075;&#6016;&#6017;&#6098;&#6040;&#6082;&#6042;</span> <i>srok khmae</i> (<small>Khmer pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Khmer" title="Help:IPA/Khmer">[srok &#712;k&#688;mae]</a></span>), meaning "Khmer\'s Land", or the slightly more formal <span lang="km" title="Khmer language text">&#6036;&#6098;&#6042;&#6033;&#6081;&#6047;&#6016;&#6040;&#6098;&#6038;&#6075;&#6023;&#6070;</span> <i>pr&#593;teih kampuci&#601;</i> (<small>Khmer pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Khmer" title="Help:IPA/Khmer">[pr&#593;.&#712;teih kam.pu.ci&#601;]</a></span>), literally "Country of Kampuchea". The name "Cambodia" is used most often in the Western world while "Kampuchea" is more widely used in the East.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" Cambodia</b></td>\n<td>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cambodia" title="History of Cambodia">History of Cambodia</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-history">Pre-history</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Early_history_of_Cambodia" title="Early history of Cambodia">Early history of Cambodia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ewer_from_Cambodia,_Angkorian_era,_12th_century,_glazed_stoneware,_HAA.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1365" data-file-width="1797" decoding="async" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Ewer_from_Cambodia%2C_Angkorian_era%2C_12th_century%2C_glazed_stoneware%2C_HAA.JPG/220px-Ewer_from_Cambodia%2C_Angkorian_era%2C_12th_century%2C_glazed_stoneware%2C_HAA.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Ewer_from_Cambodia%2C_Angkorian_era%2C_12th_century%2C_glazed_stoneware%2C_HAA.JPG/330px-Ewer_from_Cambodia%2C_Angkorian_era%2C_12th_century%2C_glazed_stoneware%2C_HAA.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Ewer_from_Cambodia%2C_Angkorian_era%2C_12th_century%2C_glazed_stoneware%2C_HAA.JPG/440px-Ewer_from_Cambodia%2C_Angkorian_era%2C_12th_century%2C_glazed_stoneware%2C_HAA.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ewer_from_Cambodia,_Angkorian_era,_12th_century,_glazed_stoneware,_HAA.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Glazed stoneware dating back to the 12th century</div></div></div>\n<p>There exists sparse evidence for a <a href="/wiki/Pleistocene" title="Pleistocene">Pleistocene</a> human occupation of present-day Cambodia, which includes <a href="/wiki/Quartz" title="Quartz">quartz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quartzite" title="Quartzite">quartzite</a> pebble tools found in terraces along the Mekong River, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stung_Treng_Province" title="Stung Treng Province">Stung Treng</a> and <a href="/wiki/Krati%C3%A9_Province" title="Krati&#233; Province">Krati&#233;</a> provinces, and in <a href="/wiki/Kampot_Province" title="Kampot Province">Kampot Province</a>, although their dating is unreliable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stark2004_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-stark2004-27">[27]</a></sup> Some slight archaeological evidence shows communities of <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherers</a> inhabited the region during <a href="/wiki/Holocene" title="Holocene">Holocene</a>: the most ancient archaeological discovery site in Cambodia is considered to be the cave of <i>L\'aang Spean</i>, in <a href="/wiki/Battambang_Province" title="Battambang Province">Battambang Province</a>, which belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Hoabinhian" title="Hoabinhian">Hoabinhian</a> period. Excavations in its lower layers produced a series of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radiocarbon" title="Radiocarbon">radiocarbon</a> dates around 6000 BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stark2004_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-stark2004-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Upper layers in the same site gave evidence of transition to <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a>, containing the earliest dated earthenware ceramics in Cambodia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Archaeological records for the period between Holocene and <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> remain equally limited. A pivotal event in Cambodian prehistory was the slow penetration of the first rice farmers from the north, which began in the late 3rd millennium BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-higham2001pre_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-higham2001pre-30">[30]</a></sup> The most curious prehistoric evidence in Cambodia are the various "circular <a href="/wiki/Earthworks_(archaeology)" title="Earthworks (archaeology)">earthworks</a>" discovered in the <a href="/wiki/Red_soil" title="Red soil">red soils</a> near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memot" title="Memot">Memot</a> and in the adjacent region of Vietnam in the latter 1950s. Their function and age are still debated, but some of them possibly date from 2nd millennium BC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bayon_Angkor_Relief1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Bayon_Angkor_Relief1.jpg/220px-Bayon_Angkor_Relief1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Bayon_Angkor_Relief1.jpg/330px-Bayon_Angkor_Relief1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Bayon_Angkor_Relief1.jpg/440px-Bayon_Angkor_Relief1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bayon_Angkor_Relief1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Khmer_Empire" title="Khmer Empire">Khmer</a> army going to war against the <a href="/wiki/Champa" title="Champa">Cham</a>, from a relief on the <a href="/wiki/Bayon" title="Bayon">Bayon</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Other prehistoric sites of somewhat uncertain date are <i>Samrong Sen</i> (not far from the ancient capital of <a href="/wiki/Oudong" title="Oudong">Oudong</a>), where the first investigations began in 1875,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-higham1989_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-higham1989-33">[33]</a></sup> and <i>Phum Snay</i>, in the northern province of <a href="/wiki/Banteay_Meanchey_Province" title="Banteay Meanchey Province">Banteay Meanchey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> An excavation at Phum Snay revealed 21 graves with iron weapons and cranial trauma which could point to conflicts in the past, possible with larger cities in Angkor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-higham2001pre_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-higham2001pre-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup>\n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Prehistoric artefacts are often found during mining activities in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ratanakiri" title="Ratanakiri">Ratanakiri</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stark2004_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-stark2004-27">[27]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Iron was worked by about 500 BC, with supporting evidence coming from the <a href="/wiki/Khorat_Plateau" title="Khorat Plateau">Khorat Plateau</a>, in modern-day Thailand. In Cambodia, some Iron Age settlements were found beneath <a href="/wiki/Baksei_Chamkrong" title="Baksei Chamkrong">Baksei Chamkrong</a> and other Angkorian temples while circular earthworks were found beneath <i>Lovea</i> a few kilometres north-west of Angkor. Burials, much richer than other types of finds, testify to improvement of food availability and trade (even on long distances: in the 4th century BC trade relations with India were already opened) and the existence of a social structure and labour organisation.\nAlso, among the artefacts from the Iron Age, glass beads are important evidence. Different kinds of glass beads recovered from several sites across Cambodia, such as the Phum Snay site in northwest and the Prohear site in southeast,  show that there were two main trading networks at the time. The two networks were separated by time and space, which indicate that there was a shift from one network to the other at about 2nd&#8211;4th century AD, probably with changes in socio-political powers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-Angkorian_and_Angkorian_era">Pre-Angkorian and Angkorian era</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Funan" title="Kingdom of Funan">Kingdom of Funan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chenla" title="Chenla">Chenla</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Empire" title="Khmer Empire">Khmer Empire</a></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angkor_Wat.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1362" data-file-width="2004" decoding="async" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Angkor_Wat.jpg/200px-Angkor_Wat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Angkor_Wat.jpg/300px-Angkor_Wat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/Angkor_Wat.jpg/400px-Angkor_Wat.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Angkor_Wat" title="Angkor Wat">Angkor Wat</a>.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bayon_Angkor_frontal.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="674" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Bayon_Angkor_frontal.jpg/200px-Bayon_Angkor_frontal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Bayon_Angkor_frontal.jpg/300px-Bayon_Angkor_frontal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Bayon_Angkor_frontal.jpg/400px-Bayon_Angkor_frontal.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Faces of <a href="/wiki/Bodhisattva" title="Bodhisattva">Bodhisattva</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avalokiteshvara" title="Avalokiteshvara">Avalokiteshvara</a> at <a href="/wiki/Bayon" title="Bayon">Prasat Bayon</a>.</div></div></div></div>\n<p>During the 3rd, 4th, and 5th centuries, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indianised_kingdom" title="Indianised kingdom">Indianised states</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Funan" title="Kingdom of Funan">Funan</a> and its successor, <a href="/wiki/Chenla" title="Chenla">Chenla</a>, coalesced in present-day Cambodia and southwestern Vietnam. For more than 2,000 years, what was to become Cambodia absorbed influences from <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, passing them on to other Southeast Asian civilisations that are now Thailand and Laos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BRIT_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-BRIT-38">[38]</a></sup> Little else is known for certain of these polities, however Chinese chronicles and tribute records do make mention of them. It is believed that the territory of Funan may have held the port known to Alexandrian geographer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Claudius_Ptolemy" title="Claudius Ptolemy">Claudius Ptolemy</a> as "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kattigara" title="Kattigara">Kattigara</a>". The Chinese chronicles suggest that after Jayavarman I of Chenla died around 690, turmoil ensued which resulted in division of the kingdom into Land Chenla and Water Chenla which was loosely ruled by weak princes under the dominion of <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Empire" title="Khmer Empire">Khmer Empire</a> grew out of these remnants of Chenla, becoming firmly established in 802 when <a href="/wiki/Jayavarman_II" title="Jayavarman II">Jayavarman II</a> (reigned c790-850) declared independence from <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a> and proclaimed himself a <a href="/wiki/Devaraja" title="Devaraja">Devaraja</a>. He and his followers instituted the cult of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/God-king" title="God-king">God-king</a> and began a series of conquests that formed an empire which flourished in the area from the 9th to the 15th centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> During the rule of <a href="/wiki/Jayavarman_VIII" title="Jayavarman VIII">Jayavarman VIII</a> the Angkor empire was attacked by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol" title="Mongol">Mongol</a> army of <a href="/wiki/Kublai_Khan" title="Kublai Khan">Kublai Khan</a>, however the king was able to buy peace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> Around the 13th century, monks from <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> introduced <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theravada_Buddhism" title="Theravada Buddhism">Theravada Buddhism</a> to Southeast Asia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> The religion spread and eventually displaced Hinduism and Mahayana Buddhism as the popular religion of Angkor; however it was not the official state religion until 1295; when <a href="/wiki/Indravarman_III" title="Indravarman III">Indravarman III</a> took power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Khmer Empire was Southeast Asia\'s largest empire during the 12th century. The empire\'s centre of power was <a href="/wiki/Angkor" title="Angkor">Angkor</a>, where a series of capitals were constructed during the empire\'s zenith. In 2007 an international team of researchers using satellite photographs and other modern techniques concluded that Angkor had been the largest pre-industrial city in the world with an urban sprawl of 2,980 square kilometres (1,151 square miles).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The city, which could have supported a population of up to one million people<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Angkor_Wat" title="Angkor Wat">Angkor Wat</a>, the best known and best-preserved religious temple at the site, still serves as a reminder of Cambodia\'s past as a major regional power. The empire, though in decline, remained a significant force in the region until its fall in the 15th century.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dark_ages_of_Cambodia">Dark ages of Cambodia</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dark_ages_of_Cambodia" title="Dark ages of Cambodia">Dark ages of Cambodia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vietnam_1760.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2790" data-file-width="2290" decoding="async" height="268" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Vietnam_1760.jpg/220px-Vietnam_1760.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Vietnam_1760.jpg/330px-Vietnam_1760.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Vietnam_1760.jpg/440px-Vietnam_1760.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vietnam_1760.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of <a href="/wiki/Indochina" title="Indochina">Indochina</a> in 1760</div></div></div>\n<p>After a long series of wars with neighbouring kingdoms, Angkor was sacked by the <a href="/wiki/Ayutthaya_Kingdom" title="Ayutthaya Kingdom">Ayutthaya Kingdom</a> and abandoned in 1432 because of ecological failure and infrastructure breakdown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chan_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chan-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> This led to a period of economic, social, and cultural stagnation when the kingdom\'s internal affairs came increasingly under the control of its neighbours. By this time, the Khmer penchant for monument building had ceased. Older faiths such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahayana_Buddhism" title="Mahayana Buddhism">Mahayana Buddhism</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> cult of the god-king had been supplanted by Theravada Buddhism.\n</p><p>The court moved the capital to <a href="/wiki/Longvek" title="Longvek">Longvek</a> where the kingdom sought to regain its glory through maritime trade.  The first mention of Cambodia in European documents was in 1511 by the <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a>. Portuguese travellers described the city as a place of flourishing wealth and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foreign_trade" title="Foreign trade">foreign trade</a>. The attempt was short-lived however, as continued wars with Ayutthaya and the Vietnamese resulted in the loss of more territory and <a href="/wiki/Siamese%E2%80%93Cambodian_War_(1591%E2%80%931594)" title="Siamese&#8211;Cambodian War (1591&#8211;1594)">Longvek being conquered and destroyed</a> by King <a href="/wiki/Naresuan" title="Naresuan">Naresuan the Great</a> of Ayutthaya in 1594. A new Khmer capital was established at <a href="/wiki/Oudong" title="Oudong">Oudong</a> south of Longvek in 1618, but its monarchs could survive only by entering into what amounted to alternating <a href="/wiki/Vassal" title="Vassal">vassal</a> relationships with the Siamese and Vietnamese for the next three centuries with only a few short-lived periods of relative independence.\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khmer_Leu" title="Khmer Leu">hill tribe</a> people in Cambodia were "hunted incessantly and carried off as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Asia" title="Slavery in Asia">slaves</a> by the Siamese (Thai), the Annamites (Vietnamese), and the Cambodians".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Attribution_needed" title="Wikipedia:Attribution needed"><span title="This sentence may contain perspectives and opinions without stating whose they are. (April 2018)">attribution needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the nineteenth century a renewed struggle between Siam and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> for control of Cambodia resulted in a period when Vietnamese officials attempted to force the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khmers" title="Khmers">Khmers</a> to adopt Vietnamese customs. This led to several rebellions against the Vietnamese and appeals to Thailand for assistance. The <a href="/wiki/Siamese%E2%80%93Vietnamese_War_(1841%E2%80%931845)" title="Siamese&#8211;Vietnamese War (1841&#8211;1845)">Siamese&#8211;Vietnamese War (1841&#8211;1845)</a> ended with an agreement to place the country under <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">joint suzerainty</a>. This later led to the signing of a treaty for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_protectorate_of_Cambodia" title="French protectorate of Cambodia">French Protection of Cambodia</a> by King <a href="/wiki/Norodom_of_Cambodia" title="Norodom of Cambodia">Norodom Prohmborirak</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_colonisation">French colonisation</span></h3>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:154px;max-width:154px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sa_Majest%C3%A9_Sisowath_Monivong.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="5007" data-file-width="2915" decoding="async" height="258" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Sa_Majest%C3%A9_Sisowath_Monivong.jpg/150px-Sa_Majest%C3%A9_Sisowath_Monivong.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Sa_Majest%C3%A9_Sisowath_Monivong.jpg/225px-Sa_Majest%C3%A9_Sisowath_Monivong.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Sa_Majest%C3%A9_Sisowath_Monivong.jpg/300px-Sa_Majest%C3%A9_Sisowath_Monivong.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left">King <a href="/wiki/Sisowath_Monivong" title="Sisowath Monivong">Sisowath Monivong</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Norodom_Sihanouk_1941.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="809" data-file-width="570" decoding="async" height="213" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Norodom_Sihanouk_1941.jpg/150px-Norodom_Sihanouk_1941.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Norodom_Sihanouk_1941.jpg/225px-Norodom_Sihanouk_1941.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Norodom_Sihanouk_1941.jpg/300px-Norodom_Sihanouk_1941.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left">Coronation of <a href="/wiki/Norodom_Sihanouk" title="Norodom Sihanouk">Norodom Sihanouk</a> in 1941</div></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1863, <a href="/wiki/Norodom_of_Cambodia" title="Norodom of Cambodia">King Norodom</a>, who had been installed by <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CHANDLER_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-CHANDLER-9">[9]</a></sup> sought the protection of Thailand from French rule. In 1867, the Thai king signed a treaty with France, renouncing <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">suzerainty</a> over Cambodia in exchange for the control of <a href="/wiki/Battambang_Province" title="Battambang Province">Battambang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siem_Reap_Province" title="Siem Reap Province">Siem Reap</a> provinces which officially became part of Thailand. The provinces were ceded back to Cambodia by a border treaty between France and Thailand in 1907.\n</p><p>Cambodia continued as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_protectorate_of_Cambodia" title="French protectorate of Cambodia">protectorate of France</a> from 1867 to 1953, administered as part of the colony of <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">French Indochina</a>, though <a href="/wiki/Japanese_occupation_of_Cambodia" title="Japanese occupation of Cambodia">occupied by the Japanese empire</a> from 1941 to 1945.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kamm_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kamm-48">[48]</a></sup> Between 1874 and 1962, the total population increased from about 946,000 to 5.7&#160;million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Population_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Population-49">[49]</a></sup> After King Norodom\'s death in 1904, France manipulated the choice of king, and Sisowath, Norodom\'s brother, was placed on the throne. The throne became vacant in 1941 with the death of Monivong, Sisowath\'s son, and France passed over Monivong\'s son, Monireth, feeling he was too independently minded. Instead, <a href="/wiki/Norodom_Sihanouk" title="Norodom Sihanouk">Norodom Sihanouk</a>, a maternal grandson of King Sisowath was enthroned. The French thought young Sihanouk would be easy to control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kamm_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kamm-48">[48]</a></sup> They were wrong, however, and under the reign of King Norodom Sihanouk, Cambodia gained independence from France on 9 November 1953.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kamm_48-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kamm-48">[48]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_and_Vietnam_War">Independence and Vietnam War</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Cambodia_(1953%E2%80%9370)" title="Kingdom of Cambodia (1953&#8211;70)">Kingdom of Cambodia (1953&#8211;70)</a></div>\n<p>Cambodia became a constitutional monarchy under King <a href="/wiki/Norodom_Sihanouk" title="Norodom Sihanouk">Norodom Sihanouk</a>. When <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">French Indochina</a> was given independence, Cambodia lost hope of regaining control over the <a href="/wiki/Mekong_Delta" title="Mekong Delta">Mekong Delta</a> as it was awarded to <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>. Formerly part of the Khmer Empire, the area had been controlled by the Vietnamese since 1698, with King <a href="/wiki/Chey_Chettha_II" title="Chey Chettha II">Chey Chettha II</a> granting the Vietnamese permission to settle in the area decades before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-50">[50]</a></sup> This remains a diplomatic sticking point with over one million ethnic Khmers (the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Krom" title="Khmer Krom">Khmer Krom</a>) still living in this region. The Khmer Rouge attempted invasions to recover the territory which, in part, led to Vietnam\'s invasion of Cambodia and deposition of the Khmer Rouge.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mao_Sihanouk.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="678" data-file-width="1119" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Mao_Sihanouk.jpg/220px-Mao_Sihanouk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Mao_Sihanouk.jpg/330px-Mao_Sihanouk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Mao_Sihanouk.jpg/440px-Mao_Sihanouk.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mao_Sihanouk.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Norodom_Sihanouk" title="Norodom Sihanouk">Norodom Sihanouk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mao_Zedong" title="Mao Zedong">Mao Zedong</a> in 1956</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1955, Sihanouk abdicated in favour of his father to participate in politics and was elected prime minister. Upon his father\'s death in 1960, Sihanouk again became head of state, taking the title of prince. As the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> progressed, Sihanouk adopted an official policy of <a href="/wiki/Neutral_country" title="Neutral country">neutrality</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>. Sihanouk allowed the Vietnamese communists to use Cambodia as a sanctuary and a supply route for their arms and other aid to their armed forces fighting in South Vietnam. This policy was perceived as humiliating by many Cambodians. In December 1967 Washington Post journalist Stanley Karnow was told by Sihanouk that if the US wanted to bomb the Vietnamese communist sanctuaries, he would not object, unless Cambodians were killed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The same message was conveyed to <a href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson" title="Lyndon B. Johnson">US President Johnson\'s</a> emissary <a href="/wiki/Chester_Bowles" title="Chester Bowles">Chester Bowles</a> in January 1968.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> However, in public Sihanouk refuted the right of the U.S. to use air strikes in Cambodia, and on 26 March he said "these criminal attacks must immediately and definitively stop". On 28 March a press conference was held and Sihanouk appealed to the international media: "I appeal to you to publicise abroad this very clear stand of Cambodia&#8212;that is, I will in any case oppose all bombings on Cambodian territory under whatever pretext." Nevertheless, the public pleas of Sihanouk were ignored and the bombing continued.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Members of the government and army became resentful of Sihanouk\'s ruling style as well as his tilt away from the United States.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Khmer_Republic_.281970.E2.80.9375.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Khmer_Republic_(1970&#8211;75)">Khmer Republic (1970&#8211;75)</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_Civil_War" title="Cambodian Civil War">Cambodian Civil War</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spiro_Agnew_in_Cambodia_1970.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2159" data-file-width="3246" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Spiro_Agnew_in_Cambodia_1970.jpg/220px-Spiro_Agnew_in_Cambodia_1970.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Spiro_Agnew_in_Cambodia_1970.jpg/330px-Spiro_Agnew_in_Cambodia_1970.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Spiro_Agnew_in_Cambodia_1970.jpg/440px-Spiro_Agnew_in_Cambodia_1970.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spiro_Agnew_in_Cambodia_1970.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Lon Nol with US Vice-President <a href="/wiki/Spiro_Agnew" title="Spiro Agnew">Spiro Agnew</a> in Phnom Penh, 1970</div></div></div>\n<p>While visiting Beijing in 1970 Sihanouk was <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_coup_of_1970" title="Cambodian coup of 1970">ousted by a military coup</a> led by Prime Minister General <a href="/wiki/Lon_Nol" title="Lon Nol">Lon Nol</a> and Prince Sisowath <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sirik_Matak" title="Sirik Matak">Sirik Matak</a>. US support for the coup remains unproven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> However, once the coup was completed, the new regime, which immediately demanded that the Vietnamese communists leave Cambodia, gained the political support of the United States. The North Vietnamese and Viet Cong forces, desperate to retain their sanctuaries and supply lines from North Vietnam, immediately launched armed attacks on the new government. The king urged his followers to help in overthrowing this government, hastening the onset of <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_Civil_War" title="Cambodian Civil War">civil war</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SIHNK_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-SIHNK-55">[55]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Soon <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a> rebels began using him to gain support. However, from 1970 until early 1972, the Cambodian conflict was largely one between the government and army of Cambodia, and the armed forces of North Vietnam. As they gained control of Cambodian territory, the Vietnamese communists imposed a new political infrastructure, which was eventually dominated by the Cambodian communists now referred to as the Khmer Rouge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>  Between 1969 and 1973, <a href="/wiki/South_Vietnam" title="South Vietnam">Republic of Vietnam</a> and US forces <a href="/wiki/Operation_Menu" title="Operation Menu">bombed</a> Cambodia in an effort to disrupt the <a href="/wiki/Viet_Cong" title="Viet Cong">Viet Cong</a> and Khmer Rouge.\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:219px;max-width:219px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:217px;max-width:217px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_aircraft_LORAN_bombing_over_Cambodia_c1973.JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="402" data-file-width="774" decoding="async" height="112" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/US_aircraft_LORAN_bombing_over_Cambodia_c1973.JPG/215px-US_aircraft_LORAN_bombing_over_Cambodia_c1973.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/US_aircraft_LORAN_bombing_over_Cambodia_c1973.JPG/323px-US_aircraft_LORAN_bombing_over_Cambodia_c1973.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/US_aircraft_LORAN_bombing_over_Cambodia_c1973.JPG/430px-US_aircraft_LORAN_bombing_over_Cambodia_c1973.JPG 2x" width="215"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left">Tens of thousands of people were killed during the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Freedom_Deal" title="Operation Freedom Deal">US bombing of Cambodia</a> between 1970 and 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:217px;max-width:217px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marines_deploy_at_LZ_Hotel.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="482" data-file-width="758" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Marines_deploy_at_LZ_Hotel.jpg/215px-Marines_deploy_at_LZ_Hotel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Marines_deploy_at_LZ_Hotel.jpg/323px-Marines_deploy_at_LZ_Hotel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Marines_deploy_at_LZ_Hotel.jpg/430px-Marines_deploy_at_LZ_Hotel.jpg 2x" width="215"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left"><a href="/wiki/Operation_Eagle_Pull" title="Operation Eagle Pull">Operation Eagle Pull</a></div></div></div></div>\n<p>Documents uncovered from the Soviet archives after 1991 reveal that the North Vietnamese attempt to overrun Cambodia in 1970 was launched at the explicit request of the Khmer Rouge and negotiated by <a href="/wiki/Pol_Pot" title="Pol Pot">Pol Pot</a>\'s then second in command, <a href="/wiki/Nuon_Chea" title="Nuon Chea">Nuon Chea</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> NVA units overran many Cambodian army positions while the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Kampuchea" title="Communist Party of Kampuchea">Communist Party of Kampuchea</a> (CPK) expanded their small-scale attacks on lines of communication. In response to the North Vietnamese invasion, US President <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a> announced that US and South Vietnamese ground forces had entered Cambodia in a campaign aimed at destroying NVA base areas in Cambodia (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cambodian_Incursion" title="Cambodian Incursion">Cambodian Incursion</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Although a considerable quantity of equipment was seized or destroyed by US and South Vietnamese forces, containment of North Vietnamese forces proved elusive.\n</p><p>The Khmer Republic\'s leadership was plagued by disunity among its three principal figures: Lon Nol, Sihanouk\'s cousin <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sirik_Matak" title="Sirik Matak">Sirik Matak</a>, and National Assembly leader <a href="/wiki/In_Tam" title="In Tam">In Tam</a>. Lon Nol remained in power in part because neither of the others was prepared to take his place. In 1972, a constitution was adopted, a parliament elected, and Lon Nol became president. But disunity, the problems of transforming a 30,000-man army into a national combat force of more than 200,000 men, and spreading corruption weakened the civilian administration and army.\n</p><p>The Communist insurgency inside Cambodia continued to grow, aided by supplies and military support from North Vietnam. Pol Pot and <a href="/wiki/Ieng_Sary" title="Ieng Sary">Ieng Sary</a> asserted their dominance over the Vietnamese-trained communists, many of whom were purged. At the same time, the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Kampuchea" title="Communist Party of Kampuchea">CPK</a> forces became stronger and more independent of their Vietnamese patrons. By 1973, the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Kampuchea" title="Communist Party of Kampuchea">CPK</a> were fighting battles against government forces with little or no North Vietnamese troop support, and they controlled nearly 60% of Cambodia\'s territory and 25% of its population. The government made three unsuccessful attempts to enter into negotiations with the insurgents, but by 1974, the <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Kampuchea" title="Communist Party of Kampuchea">CPK</a> were operating openly as divisions, and some of the NVA combat forces had moved into South Vietnam. Lon Nol\'s control was reduced to small enclaves around the cities and main transportation routes. More than 2 million refugees from the war lived in <a href="/wiki/Phnom_Penh" title="Phnom Penh">Phnom Penh</a> and other cities.\n</p><p>On New Year\'s Day 1975, Communist troops launched an offensive which, in 117 days of the hardest fighting of the war, collapsed the Khmer Republic. Simultaneous attacks around the perimeter of Phnom Penh pinned down Republican forces, while other <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Kampuchea" title="Communist Party of Kampuchea">CPK</a> units overran fire bases controlling the vital lower Mekong resupply route. A US-funded airlift of ammunition and rice ended when Congress refused additional aid for Cambodia. The Lon Nol government in Phnom Penh surrendered on 17 April 1975, just five days after the US mission evacuated Cambodia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Khmer_Rouge_regime.2C_1975.E2.80.931978"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Khmer_Rouge_regime,_1975&#8211;1978">Khmer Rouge regime, 1975&#8211;1978</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Kampuchea" title="Democratic Kampuchea">Democratic Kampuchea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TuolSlang3.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="384" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/TuolSlang3.jpg/220px-TuolSlang3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/TuolSlang3.jpg/330px-TuolSlang3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/TuolSlang3.jpg/440px-TuolSlang3.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TuolSlang3.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rooms of the <a href="/wiki/Tuol_Sleng_Genocide_Museum" title="Tuol Sleng Genocide Museum">Tuol Sleng Genocide Museum</a> contain thousands of photos taken by the Khmer Rouge of their victims.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Buddhist_Stupa_at_Choeung_Ek_killing_fields,_Cambodia.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2432" data-file-width="3648" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Buddhist_Stupa_at_Choeung_Ek_killing_fields%2C_Cambodia.JPG/220px-Buddhist_Stupa_at_Choeung_Ek_killing_fields%2C_Cambodia.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Buddhist_Stupa_at_Choeung_Ek_killing_fields%2C_Cambodia.JPG/330px-Buddhist_Stupa_at_Choeung_Ek_killing_fields%2C_Cambodia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Buddhist_Stupa_at_Choeung_Ek_killing_fields%2C_Cambodia.JPG/440px-Buddhist_Stupa_at_Choeung_Ek_killing_fields%2C_Cambodia.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Buddhist_Stupa_at_Choeung_Ek_killing_fields,_Cambodia.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Choeung_Ek" title="Choeung Ek">Choeung Ek</a>, a known site of mass grave for genocide victims during the Khmer Rouge era</div></div></div>\n<p>The Khmer Rouge reached <a href="/wiki/Phnom_Penh" title="Phnom Penh">Phnom Penh</a> and took power in 1975. Led by <a href="/wiki/Pol_Pot" title="Pol Pot">Pol Pot</a>, they changed the official name of the country to <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Kampuchea" title="Democratic Kampuchea">Democratic Kampuchea</a>. The new regime modelled itself on Maoist China during the <a href="/wiki/Great_Leap_Forward" title="Great Leap Forward">Great Leap Forward</a>, immediately evacuated the cities, and sent the entire population on forced marches to rural work projects. They attempted to rebuild the country\'s agriculture on the model of the 11th century, discarded Western medicine and destroyed temples, libraries, and anything considered Western.\n</p><p>Estimates as to how many people were killed by the Khmer Rouge regime range from approximately one to three million; the most commonly cited figure is two million (about a quarter of the population).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heuveline,_Patrick_2001_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-Heuveline,_Patrick_2001-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marek_Sliwinski_1995_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marek_Sliwinski_1995-63">[63]</a></sup> This era gave rise to the term <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Killing_Fields" title="Killing Fields">Killing Fields</a>, and the prison <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tuol_Sleng" title="Tuol Sleng">Tuol Sleng</a> became notorious for its history of mass killing. Hundreds of thousands fled across the border into neighbouring Thailand. The regime disproportionately targeted <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Cambodia" title="Ethnic groups in Cambodia">ethnic minority</a> groups. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cham_(Asia)" title="Cham (Asia)">Cham</a> Muslims suffered serious purges with as much as half of their population exterminated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Pol Pot was determined to keep his power and disenfranchise any enemies or potential threats, and thus increased his violent and aggressive actions against his people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Forced repatriation in 1970 and deaths during the Khmer Rouge era reduced the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vietnamese_Cambodian" title="Vietnamese Cambodian">Vietnamese</a> population in Cambodia from between 250,000 and 300,000 in 1969 to a reported 56,000 in 1984.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Population_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-Population-49">[49]</a></sup> However, most of the victims of the Khmer Rouge regime were not ethnic minorities but ethnic Khmer. Professionals, such as doctors, lawyers and teachers, were also targeted. According to <a href="/wiki/Robert_D._Kaplan" title="Robert D. Kaplan">Robert D. Kaplan</a>, "eyeglasses were as deadly as the <a href="/wiki/Yellow_badge" title="Yellow badge">yellow star</a>" as they were seen as a sign of intellectualism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kaplan_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-kaplan-66">[66]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Religious institutions were not spared by the Khmer Rouge either. <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">Religion</a> was so viciously persecuted to such a terrifying extent that the vast majority of <a href="/wiki/Khmer_architecture" title="Khmer architecture">Cambodia\'s historic architecture</a>, 95% of Cambodia\'s Buddhist temples, was completely destroyed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Vietnamese_occupation_and_transition.2C_1978.E2.80.931992"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Vietnamese_occupation_and_transition,_1978&#8211;1992">Vietnamese occupation and transition, 1978&#8211;1992</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Kampuchea" title="People\'s Republic of Kampuchea">People\'s Republic of Kampuchea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cambodian%E2%80%93Vietnamese_War" title="Cambodian&#8211;Vietnamese War">Cambodian&#8211;Vietnamese War</a></div>\n<p>In November 1978, Vietnamese troops <a href="/wiki/Cambodian%E2%80%93Vietnamese_War" title="Cambodian&#8211;Vietnamese War">invaded Cambodia</a> in response to border raids by the Khmer Rouge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CGG_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-CGG-68">[68]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Kampuchea" title="People\'s Republic of Kampuchea">People\'s Republic of Kampuchea</a> (PRK), a <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">pro-Soviet</a> state led by the Kampuchean People\'s Revolutionary Party, a party created by the Vietnamese in 1951, and led by a group of Khmer Rouge who had fled Cambodia to avoid being purged by Pol Pot and Ta Mok, was established.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (January 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> It was fully beholden to the occupying Vietnamese army and under direction of the Vietnamese ambassador to Phnom Penh. Its arms came from Vietnam and the Soviet Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Daniel_Bultmann_2015_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-Daniel_Bultmann_2015-70">[70]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In opposition to the newly created state, a government-in-exile referred to as the <a href="/wiki/Coalition_Government_of_Democratic_Kampuchea" title="Coalition Government of Democratic Kampuchea">Coalition Government of Democratic Kampuchea</a> (CGDK) was formed in 1981 from three factions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Daniel_Bultmann_2015_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-Daniel_Bultmann_2015-70">[70]</a></sup> This consisted of the Khmer Rouge, a royalist faction led by Sihanouk, and the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_People%27s_National_Liberation_Front" title="Khmer People\'s National Liberation Front">Khmer People\'s National Liberation Front</a>. Its credentials were recognised by the United Nations. The Khmer Rouge representative to the UN, Thiounn Prasith, was retained, but he had to work in consultation with representatives of the noncommunist Cambodian parties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup>  The refusal of Vietnam to withdraw from Cambodia led to <a href="/wiki/Economic_sanctions" title="Economic sanctions">economic sanctions</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> by the US and its allies.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources"><span title="Statement needs to be more specific about the content to which it refers. (September 2012)">specify</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Modern_Cambodia#Peace_efforts_and_the_free_elections" title="Modern Cambodia">Peace efforts</a> began in Paris in 1989 under the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Kampuchea#Transition:_State_of_Cambodia_(1989_-_1993)" title="People\'s Republic of Kampuchea">State of Cambodia</a>, culminating two years later in October 1991 in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1991_Paris_Peace_Accords" title="1991 Paris Peace Accords">Paris Comprehensive Peace Settlement</a>. The UN was given a mandate to enforce a ceasefire and deal with refugees and disarmament known as the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Transitional_Authority_in_Cambodia" title="United Nations Transitional Authority in Cambodia">United Nations Transitional Authority in Cambodia</a> (UNTAC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USDOS3_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-USDOS3-74">[74]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Restoration_of_the_monarchy">Restoration of the monarchy</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:King_Norodom_Sihanouk%27s_funeral_procession_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="671" data-file-width="1100" decoding="async" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/King_Norodom_Sihanouk%27s_funeral_procession_01.jpg/220px-King_Norodom_Sihanouk%27s_funeral_procession_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/King_Norodom_Sihanouk%27s_funeral_procession_01.jpg/330px-King_Norodom_Sihanouk%27s_funeral_procession_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/King_Norodom_Sihanouk%27s_funeral_procession_01.jpg/440px-King_Norodom_Sihanouk%27s_funeral_procession_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:King_Norodom_Sihanouk%27s_funeral_procession_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>King-Father <a href="/wiki/Norodom_Sihanouk" title="Norodom Sihanouk">Norodom Sihanouk</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Death_and_state_funeral_of_Norodom_Sihanouk" title="Death and state funeral of Norodom Sihanouk">funeral procession</a> in 17 October 2012</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1993, <a href="/wiki/Norodom_Sihanouk" title="Norodom Sihanouk">Norodom Sihanouk</a> was restored as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_Cambodia" title="King of Cambodia">King of Cambodia</a>, but all power was in the hands of the government established after the UNTAC sponsored elections. The stability established following the conflict was shaken in 1997 by a <a href="/wiki/1997_clashes_in_Cambodia" title="1997 clashes in Cambodia">coup d\'&#233;tat</a> led by the co-Prime Minister Hun Sen against the non-communist parties in the government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97COUP_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-97COUP-75">[75]</a></sup> In recent years, reconstruction efforts have progressed and led to some political stability through a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multiparty</a> democracy under a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIACB_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-CIACB-1">[1]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2010, <a href="/wiki/Kang_Kek_Iew" title="Kang Kek Iew">Kang Kek Iew</a> was the first Khmer Rouge member found guilty of <a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">war crimes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a> in his role as the former commandant of the S21 extermination camp and he was sentenced to life in prison.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> However, Hun Sen has opposed extensive trials of former Khmer Rouge mass murderers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In August 2014, a UN-backed war crimes tribunal, the Extraordinary Chambers in the Courts of Cambodia (also known as the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge_Tribunal" title="Khmer Rouge Tribunal">Khmer Rouge Tribunal</a>), sentenced Khieu Samphan, the regime\'s 83-year-old former head of state, and Nuon Chea, its 88-year-old chief ideologue, to life in prison on war crimes charges for their role in the country\'s terror period in the 1970s. The trial began in November 2011. Former Foreign Minister Ieng Sary died in 2013, while his wife, Social Affairs Minister Ieng Thirith, was deemed unfit to stand trial due to dementia in 2012. The group\'s top leader, <a href="/wiki/Pol_Pot" title="Pol Pot">Pol Pot</a>, died in 1998.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Cambodia" title="Geography of Cambodia">Geography of Cambodia</a></div>\n<p>Cambodia has an area of 181,035 square kilometres (69,898 square miles) and lies entirely within the tropics, between latitudes <a href="/wiki/10th_parallel_north" title="10th parallel north">10&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/15th_parallel_north" title="15th parallel north">15&#176;N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/102nd_meridian_east" title="102nd meridian east">102&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/108th_meridian_east" title="108th meridian east">108&#176;E</a>. It borders Thailand to the north and west, Laos to the northeast, and <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> to the east and southeast. It has a 443-kilometre (275-mile) coastline along the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Thailand" title="Gulf of Thailand">Gulf of Thailand</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cambodia_Regions_Map.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2207" data-file-width="2499" decoding="async" height="353" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Cambodia_Regions_Map.png/400px-Cambodia_Regions_Map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Cambodia_Regions_Map.png/600px-Cambodia_Regions_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/Cambodia_Regions_Map.png/800px-Cambodia_Regions_Map.png 2x" width="400"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cambodia_Regions_Map.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Regional map of Cambodia</div></div></div>\n<p>Cambodia\'s landscape is characterised by a low-lying central plain that is surrounded by uplands and low mountains and includes the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tonle_Sap" title="Tonle Sap">Tonle Sap</a> (Great Lake) and the upper reaches of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mekong_River" title="Mekong River">Mekong River</a> delta. Extending outward from this central region are transitional plains, thinly forested and rising to elevations of about 650 feet (200 metres) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_sea_level" title="Above sea level">above sea level</a>.\n</p><p>To the north the Cambodian plain abuts a sandstone escarpment, which forms a southward-facing cliff stretching more than 200 miles (320 kilometres) from west to east and rising abruptly above the plain to heights of 600&#160;to 1,800 feet (180&#8211;550 metres). This cliff marks the southern limit of the <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A2ngr%C3%AAk_Mountains" title="D&#226;ngr&#234;k Mountains">D&#226;ngr&#234;k Mountains</a>.\n</p><p>Flowing south through the country\'s eastern regions is the Mekong River. East of the Mekong the transitional plains gradually merge with the eastern highlands, a region of forested mountains and high plateaus that extend into Laos and Vietnam. In southwestern Cambodia two distinct upland blocks, the <a href="/wiki/Cardamom_Mountains" title="Cardamom Mountains">Kr&#226;vanh Mountains</a> and the <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A2mrei_Mountains" title="D&#226;mrei Mountains">D&#226;mrei Mountains</a>, form another highland region that covers much of the land area between the Tonle Sap and the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Thailand" title="Gulf of Thailand">Gulf of Thailand</a>.\n</p><p>In this remote and largely uninhabited area, <a href="/wiki/Phnom_Aural" title="Phnom Aural">Phnom Aural</a>, Cambodia\'s highest peak rises to an elevation of 5,949 feet (1,813 metres).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The southern coastal region adjoining the Gulf of Thailand is a narrow lowland strip, heavily wooded and sparsely populated, which is isolated from the central plain by the southwestern highlands.\n</p><p>The most distinctive geographical feature is the inundations of the Tonle Sap, measuring about 2,590 square kilometres (1,000 square miles) during the dry season and expanding to about 24,605 square kilometres (9,500 square miles) during the rainy season. This densely populated plain, which is devoted to wet rice cultivation, is the heartland of Cambodia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-81">[81]</a></sup> Much of this area has been designated as a <a href="/wiki/Man_and_the_Biosphere_Programme" title="Man and the Biosphere Programme">biosphere reserve</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>\n<p>Cambodia\'s climate, like that of the rest of Southeast Asia, is dominated by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monsoons" title="Monsoons">monsoons</a>, which are known as tropical wet and dry because of the distinctly marked seasonal differences.\n</p><p>Cambodia has a temperature range from 21 to 35&#160;&#176;C (70 to 95&#160;&#176;F) and experiences tropical monsoons. Southwest monsoons blow inland bringing moisture-laden winds from the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Thailand" title="Gulf of Thailand">Gulf of Thailand</a> and Indian Ocean from May to October. The northeast monsoon ushers in the dry season, which lasts from November to April. The country experiences the heaviest precipitation from September to October with the driest period occurring from January to February.\n</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Development_Research_Centre" title="International Development Research Centre">International Development Research Center</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_United_Nations" title="The United Nations">The United Nations</a>, Cambodia is considered Southeast Asia\'s most vulnerable country to the effects of climate change, alongside the Philippines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Rural coastal populations are particularly at risk. Shortages of clean water, extreme flooding, mudslides, higher sea levels and potentially destructive storms are of particular concern, according to the <a class="external text" href="http://www.camclimate.org.kh/en/" rel="nofollow">Cambodia Climate Change Alliance</a>.\n</p><p>Cambodia has two distinct seasons. The rainy season, which runs from May to October, can see temperatures drop to 22&#160;&#176;C (72&#160;&#176;F) and is generally accompanied with high humidity. The dry season lasts from November to April when temperatures can rise up to 40&#160;&#176;C (104&#160;&#176;F) around April. Disastrous flooding occurred in 2001 and again in 2002, with some degree of flooding almost every year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Cambodia" title="Wildlife of Cambodia">Wildlife of Cambodia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macaques_dans_le_parc_dAngkor_Vat_(6931909635).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Macaques_dans_le_parc_dAngkor_Vat_%286931909635%29.jpg/220px-Macaques_dans_le_parc_dAngkor_Vat_%286931909635%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Macaques_dans_le_parc_dAngkor_Vat_%286931909635%29.jpg/330px-Macaques_dans_le_parc_dAngkor_Vat_%286931909635%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Macaques_dans_le_parc_dAngkor_Vat_%286931909635%29.jpg/440px-Macaques_dans_le_parc_dAngkor_Vat_%286931909635%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macaques_dans_le_parc_dAngkor_Vat_(6931909635).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macaques" title="Macaques">Macaques</a> at <a href="/wiki/Angkor" title="Angkor">Angkor</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Cambodia\'s <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> is largely founded on its <a href="/wiki/Seasonal_tropical_forest" title="Seasonal tropical forest">seasonal tropical forests</a>, containing some <a href="/wiki/List_of_trees_of_Cambodia" title="List of trees of Cambodia">180 recorded tree species</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riparian" title="Riparian">riparian</a> ecosystems. There are 212 <a href="/wiki/Mammal" title="Mammal">mammal</a> species, 536 bird species, 240 <a href="/wiki/Reptile" title="Reptile">reptile</a> species, 850 freshwater fish species (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tonle_Sap" title="Tonle Sap">Tonle Sap</a> Lake area), and 435 marine fish species recorded by science. Much of this biodiversity is contained around the Tonle Sap Lake and the surrounding biosphere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tonle_Sap_Biosphere_Reserve" title="Tonle Sap Biosphere Reserve">Tonle Sap Biosphere Reserve</a> is a reserve surrounding the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tonle_Sap" title="Tonle Sap">Tonle Sap</a> lake. It encompasses the lake and nine provinces: <a href="/wiki/Kampong_Thom_Province" title="Kampong Thom Province">Kampong Thom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siem_Reap_Province" title="Siem Reap Province">Siem Reap</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battambang_Province" title="Battambang Province">Battambang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pursat_Province" title="Pursat Province">Pursat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kampong_Chhnang_Province" title="Kampong Chhnang Province">Kampong Chhnang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banteay_Meanchey_Province" title="Banteay Meanchey Province">Banteay Meanchey</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pailin" title="Pailin">Pailin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oddar_Meanchey_Province" title="Oddar Meanchey Province">Oddar Meanchey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Preah_Vihear_Province" title="Preah Vihear Province">Preah Vihear</a>. In 1997, it was successfully nominated as a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biosphere_Reserve" title="Biosphere Reserve">Biosphere Reserve</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> Other key habitats include the dry forest of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mondolkiri" title="Mondolkiri">Mondolkiri</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ratanakiri" title="Ratanakiri">Ratanakiri</a> provinces and the <a href="/wiki/Cardamom_Mountains" title="Cardamom Mountains">Cardamom Mountains</a> ecosystem, including Bokor National Park, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Botum-Sakor_National_Park" title="Botum-Sakor National Park">Botum-Sakor National Park</a>, and the Phnom Aural and Phnom Samkos wildlife sanctuaries.\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Worldwide_Fund_for_Nature" title="Worldwide Fund for Nature">Worldwide Fund for Nature</a> recognises six distinct <a
