class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terrestrial_ecoregions" title="Terrestrial ecoregions">terrestrial ecoregions</a> in Cambodia &#8211; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardamom_Mountains_rain_forests" title="Cardamom Mountains rain forests">Cardamom Mountains rain forests</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Indochina_dry_forest" title="Central Indochina dry forest">Central Indochina dry forest</a>, Southeast Indochina dry evergreen forest, Southern <a href="/wiki/Annamite_Range" title="Annamite Range">Annamite Range</a> tropical forest, Tonle Sap freshwater swamp forest, and Tonle Sap-Mekong peat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swamp_forest" title="Swamp forest">swamp forest</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cascade_de_la_rivi%C3%A8re_sacr%C3%A9e_(Phnom_Kulen)_(6825025205).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="1365" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Cascade_de_la_rivi%C3%A8re_sacr%C3%A9e_%28Phnom_Kulen%29_%286825025205%29.jpg/220px-Cascade_de_la_rivi%C3%A8re_sacr%C3%A9e_%28Phnom_Kulen%29_%286825025205%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Cascade_de_la_rivi%C3%A8re_sacr%C3%A9e_%28Phnom_Kulen%29_%286825025205%29.jpg/330px-Cascade_de_la_rivi%C3%A8re_sacr%C3%A9e_%28Phnom_Kulen%29_%286825025205%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Cascade_de_la_rivi%C3%A8re_sacr%C3%A9e_%28Phnom_Kulen%29_%286825025205%29.jpg/440px-Cascade_de_la_rivi%C3%A8re_sacr%C3%A9e_%28Phnom_Kulen%29_%286825025205%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cascade_de_la_rivi%C3%A8re_sacr%C3%A9e_(Phnom_Kulen)_(6825025205).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Waterfall at <a href="/wiki/Phnom_Kulen" title="Phnom Kulen">Phnom Kulen</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Cambodia has a bad but improving performance in the global <a href="/wiki/Environmental_Performance_Index" title="Environmental Performance Index">Environmental Performance Index</a> (EPI) with an overall ranking of 146 out of 180 countries in 2016. This is among the worst in the <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asian</a> region, only ahead of Laos and Myanmar. The EPI was established in 2001 by the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a> as a global gauge to measure how well individual countries perform in implementing the United Nations\' <a href="/wiki/Sustainable_Development_Goals" title="Sustainable Development Goals">Sustainable Development Goals</a>. The environmental areas where Cambodia performs worst (i.e. highest ranking) are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_quality" title="Air quality">air quality</a> (148), <a href="/wiki/Water_resource_management" title="Water resource management">water resource management</a> (140) and health impacts of environmental issues (137), with the areas of <a href="/wiki/Sanitation" title="Sanitation">sanitation</a>, environmental impacts of fisheries and forest management following closely. Cambodia performs best when it comes to handling the <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_cycle" title="Nitrogen cycle">nitrogen balance</a> in the agricultural industry specifically, an area where Cambodia excels and are among the best in the world. In addition, Cambodia has an unusually large area of wildlife protections, both on land and at sea, with the land-based protections covering about 20% of the country. This secures Cambodia a better than average ranking of 61 in relation to biodiversity and habitat, even though illegal logging, construction and poaching are heavily deteriorating these protections and habitats in reality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GreenList_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-GreenList-90">[90]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prey_Lang_Forest_Aerial.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2912" data-file-width="4368" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Prey_Lang_Forest_Aerial.jpg/220px-Prey_Lang_Forest_Aerial.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Prey_Lang_Forest_Aerial.jpg/330px-Prey_Lang_Forest_Aerial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Prey_Lang_Forest_Aerial.jpg/440px-Prey_Lang_Forest_Aerial.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Prey_Lang_Forest_Aerial.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Prey_Lang" title="Prey Lang">Prey Lang Forest</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The rate of <a href="/wiki/Deforestation_in_Cambodia" title="Deforestation in Cambodia">deforestation in Cambodia</a> is one of the highest in the world and it is often perceived as the most destructive, singular environmental issue in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GreenList_90-1"><a href="#cite_note-GreenList-90">[90]</a></sup> Cambodia\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_forest" title="Primary forest">primary forest</a> cover fell from over 70% in 1969 to just 3.1% in 2007. In total, Cambodia lost 25,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (9,700&#160;sq&#160;mi) of forest between 1990 and 2005 &#8211; 3,340&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (1,290&#160;sq&#160;mi) of which was primary forest. Since 2007, less than 3,220&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (1,243&#160;sq&#160;mi) of primary forest remain with the result that the future <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainability</a> of the forest reserves of Cambodia is under severe threat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> In 2010&#8211;2015, the annual rate of deforestation was 1.3%. The environmental degradation also includes national parks and wildlife sanctuaries on a large scale and many endangered and endemic species are now threatened with extinction due to loss of habitats. There are many reasons for the deforestation in Cambodia, which range from opportunistic <a href="/wiki/Illegal_logging" title="Illegal logging">illegal loggings</a> to large scale clearings from big construction projects and agricultural activities. The global issue of <a href="/wiki/Land_grabbing" title="Land grabbing">land grabbing</a> is particularly rampant in Cambodia. The deforestation involves the local population, Cambodian businesses and authorities as well as transnational corporations from all over the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Plans for <a href="/wiki/Hydropower_in_the_Mekong_River_Basin" title="Hydropower in the Mekong River Basin">hydroelectric development</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Mekong_Subregion" title="Greater Mekong Subregion">Greater Mekong Subregion</a>, by <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a> in particular, pose a "real danger to the food supply of <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> and Cambodia. Upstream dams will imperil the fish stocks that provide the vast majority of Cambodia\'s protein and could also denude the Mekong River of the silt Vietnam needs for its rice basket."\nThe rich fisheries of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tonle_Sap" title="Tonle Sap">Tonle Sap</a>, the largest freshwater lake in <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>, largely supply the impoverished country\'s protein. The lake is unusual: It all but disappears in the dry season and then expands massively as water flow from the Mekong backs up when the rains come. "Those fish are so important for their livelihoods, both economically and nutritionally", said Gordon Holtgrieve, a professor at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Washington" title="University of Washington">University of Washington</a> who researches Cambodia\'s freshwater fish and he points out that none of the dams that are either built or being built on the Mekong river "are pointing at good outcomes for the fisheries".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the 2010s, the Cambodian government and educational system has increased its involvement and co-operation with both national and international environmental groups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> A new National Environmental Strategy and Action Plan (NESAP) for Cambodia is to be implemented from late 2016 to 2023 and contains new ideas for how to incite a <a href="/wiki/Green_growth" title="Green growth">green</a> and environmentally <a href="/wiki/Sustainability" title="Sustainability">sustainable</a> growth for the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2017, the U.S. cut funds to help clear <a href="/wiki/Unexploded_ordnance" title="Unexploded ordnance">unexploded ordnance</a> including land mines and chemical weapons in Cambodia which it had dropped during the Vietnam War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Cambodia" title="Politics of Cambodia">Politics of Cambodia</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_Cambodia" title="List of political parties in Cambodia">List of political parties in Cambodia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Cambodian_protests" title="2013&#8211;14 Cambodian protests">2013&#8211;14 Cambodian protests</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Norodom_king_of_Cambodia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="798" decoding="async" height="331" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Norodom_king_of_Cambodia.jpg/220px-Norodom_king_of_Cambodia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Norodom_king_of_Cambodia.jpg/330px-Norodom_king_of_Cambodia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Norodom_king_of_Cambodia.jpg/440px-Norodom_king_of_Cambodia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Norodom_king_of_Cambodia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Norodom_Sihamoni" title="Norodom Sihamoni">Norodom Sihamoni</a>, King of Cambodia</div></div></div>\n<p>National politics in Cambodia take place within the framework of the nation\'s constitution of 1993. The government is a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> operated as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Cambodia" title="Prime Minister of Cambodia">Prime Minister of Cambodia</a>, an office held by <a href="/wiki/Hun_Sen" title="Hun Sen">Hun Sen</a> since 1985, is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, while the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_of_Cambodia" title="King of Cambodia">King of Cambodia</a> (currently <a href="/wiki/Norodom_Sihamoni" title="Norodom Sihamoni">Norodom Sihamoni</a>) is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>. The prime minister is appointed by the king, on the advice and with the approval of the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Cambodia" title="National Assembly of Cambodia">National Assembly</a>. The prime minister and the ministerial appointees exercise <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Executive_power" title="Executive power">executive power</a>.\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislative_power" title="Legislative power">Legislative powers</a> are shared by the executive and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicameral" title="Bicameral">bicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Cambodia" title="Parliament of Cambodia">Parliament of Cambodia</a> (<span lang="km" title="Khmer language text">&#6047;&#6039;&#6070;&#6031;&#6086;&#6030;&#6070;&#6020;&#6042;&#6070;&#6047;&#6098;&#6031;&#6098;&#6042;</span>, <i>saphea damnang reastr</i>), which consists of a lower house, the National Assembly (<span lang="km" title="Khmer language text">&#6042;&#6026;&#6098;&#6027;&#6047;&#6039;&#6070;</span>, <i>rotsaphea</i>) and an upper house, the Senate (<span lang="km" title="Khmer language text">&#6038;&#6098;&#6042;&#6073;&#6033;&#6098;&#6034;&#6047;&#6039;&#6070;</span>, <i>protsaphea</i>). Members of the 123-seat Assembly are elected through a system of <a href="/wiki/Proportional_representation" title="Proportional representation">proportional representation</a> and serve for a maximum term of five years. The Senate has 61 seats, two of which are appointed by the king and two others by the National Assembly, and the rest elected by the <a href="/wiki/Commune_council" title="Commune council">commune councillors</a> from 24 <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Cambodia" title="Provinces of Cambodia">provinces of Cambodia</a>. Senators serve six-year terms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 14 October 2004, King <a href="/wiki/Norodom_Sihamoni" title="Norodom Sihamoni">Norodom Sihamoni</a> was selected by a special nine-member <a href="/wiki/Royal_Council_of_the_Throne" title="Royal Council of the Throne">Royal Throne Council</a>, part of a selection process that was quickly put in place after the abdication of King <a href="/wiki/Norodom_Sihanouk" title="Norodom Sihanouk">Norodom Sihanouk</a> a week prior. Sihamoni\'s selection was endorsed by Prime Minister Hun Sen and National Assembly Speaker Prince <a href="/wiki/Norodom_Ranariddh" title="Norodom Ranariddh">Norodom Ranariddh</a> (the king\'s half-brother and current chief advisor), both members of the throne council. He was enthroned in Phnom Penh on 29 October 2004.\n</p><p>Officially a multiparty democracy, in reality "the country remains a one-party state dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_People%27s_Party" title="Cambodian People\'s Party">Cambodian People\'s Party</a> and Prime Minister Hun Sen, a recast <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a> official in power since 1985. The open doors to new investment during his reign have yielded the most access to a coterie of cronies of his and his wife, <a href="/wiki/Bun_Rany" title="Bun Rany">Bun Rany</a>."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Attribution_needed" title="Wikipedia:Attribution needed"><span title="This sentence may contain perspectives and opinions without stating whose they are. (July 2018)">attribution needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Cambodia\'s government has been described by the Human Rights Watch\'s Southeast Asian director, David Roberts, as a "vaguely communist free-market state with a relatively authoritarian coalition ruling over a superficial democracy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-17">[17]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Prime Minister Hun Sen has vowed to rule until he is 74.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> He is a former Khmer Rouge member who defected. His government is regularly accused of ignoring human rights and suppressing political dissent. The 2013 election results were disputed by Hun Sen\'s opposition, leading to demonstrations in the capital. Demonstrators were injured and killed in Phnom Penh where a reported 20,000 protesters gathered, with some clashing with riot police.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> From a humble farming background, Hun Sen was just 33 when he took power in 1985, and is by some considered a long ruling <a href="/wiki/Dictator" title="Dictator">dictator</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="center">\n<table>\n<tbody><tr>\n<td valign="top">\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cambodia_2011_monuments_28.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3168" data-file-width="4752" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Cambodia_2011_monuments_28.jpg/210px-Cambodia_2011_monuments_28.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Cambodia_2011_monuments_28.jpg/315px-Cambodia_2011_monuments_28.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Cambodia_2011_monuments_28.jpg/420px-Cambodia_2011_monuments_28.jpg 2x" width="210"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cambodia_2011_monuments_28.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Head of State</div></div></div>\n</td>\n<td valign="top">\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cambodian_Peace_Palace.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1333" data-file-width="2000" decoding="async" height="140" href="/wiki/File:Cambodian_Peace_Palace.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Head of Government</div></div></div>\n</td>\n<td valign="top">\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cambodian_National_Assembly_2016-7.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3045" data-file-width="4569" decoding="async" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Cambodian_National_Assembly_2016-7.jpg/315px-Cambodian_National_Assembly_2016-7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Cambodian_National_Assembly_2016-7.jpg/420px-Cambodian_National_Assembly_2016-7.jpg 2x" width="210"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cambodian_National_Assembly_2016-7.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Parliament</div></div></div>\n</td>\n<td valign="top">\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:212px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2016_Phnom_Penh,_Budynek_s%C4%85du_(04).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3395" data-file-width="4988" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/2016_Phnom_Penh%2C_Budynek_s%C4%85du_%2804%29.jpg/210px-2016_Phnom_Penh%2C_Budynek_s%C4%85du_%2804%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/2016_Phnom_Penh%2C_Budynek_s%C4%85du_%2804%29.jpg/315px-2016_Phnom_Penh%2C_Budynek_s%C4%85du_%2804%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/2016_Phnom_Penh%2C_Budynek_s%C4%85du_%2804%29.jpg/420px-2016_Phnom_Penh%2C_Budynek_s%C4%85du_%2804%29.jpg 2x" width="210"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2016_Phnom_Penh,_Budynek_s%C4%85du_(04).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Supreme Court</div></div></div>\n</td>\n<td valign="top">\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_People%27s_Party" title="Cambodian People\'s Party">Cambodian People\'s Party</a> (CPP) is the sole dominant-party in Cambodia. Since 2018, the CPP commands all but four seats in <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Cambodia" title="Parliament of Cambodia">Parliament</a>, including all 125 seats in the National Assembly and 58 of 62 seats in the Senate.\n</p>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:154px;max-width:154px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hun_Sen_(2016)_cropped.jpg"><img alt="Portrait" data-file-height="552" data-file-width="414" decoding="async" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Hun_Sen_%282016%29_cropped.jpg/150px-Hun_Sen_%282016%29_cropped.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Hun_Sen_%282016%29_cropped.jpg/225px-Hun_Sen_%282016%29_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Hun_Sen_%282016%29_cropped.jpg/300px-Hun_Sen_%282016%29_cropped.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Hun_Sen" title="Hun Sen">Hun Sen</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Hun Sen and his government have seen much controversy. Hun Sen was a former Khmer Rouge commander who was originally installed by the Vietnamese and, after the Vietnamese left the country, maintains his <a href="/wiki/Strongman_(politics)" title="Strongman (politics)">strong man</a> position by violence and oppression when deemed necessary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HRWAdams_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-HRWAdams-107">[107]</a></sup> In 1997, fearing the growing power of his co&#8211;prime minister, Prince Norodom Ranariddh, Hun launched a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1997_Cambodian_Coup" title="1997 Cambodian Coup">coup</a>, using the army to purge Ranariddh and his supporters. Ranariddh was ousted and fled to Paris while other opponents of Hun Sen were arrested, tortured, and some summarily executed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HRWAdams_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-HRWAdams-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In addition to <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Cambodia" title="Human rights in Cambodia">political oppression</a>, the Cambodian government has been accused of corruption in the sale of vast areas of land to foreign investors resulting in the eviction of thousands of villagers<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> as well as taking bribes in exchange for grants to exploit Cambodia\'s oil wealth and mineral resources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Cambodia is consistently listed as one of the most corrupt governments in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> currently recognises one <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_conscience" title="Prisoner of conscience">prisoner of conscience</a> in the country: 33-year-old land rights activist <a href="/wiki/Yorm_Bopha" title="Yorm Bopha">Yorm Bopha</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yorm_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-yorm-114">[114]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Journalists covering a protest over disputed election results in Phnom Penh on 22 September 2013 say they were deliberately attacked by police and men in plain clothes, with slingshots and stun guns. The attack against the president of the Overseas Press Club of Cambodia, Rick Valenzuela, was captured on video.\nThe violence came amid political tensions as the opposition boycotted the opening of <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">Parliament</a> due to concerns about electoral fraud. Seven reporters sustained minor injuries while at least two Cambodian protesters were hit by slingshot projectiles and hospitalized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2017 the Cambodia\'s Supreme Court dissolved the main opposition party, <a href="/wiki/Cambodia_National_Rescue_Party" title="Cambodia National Rescue Party">Cambodia National Rescue Party</a> (CNRP), paving the way for a return to a yet more authoritarian political system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption">Corruption</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_Cambodia" title="Corruption in Cambodia">Corruption in Cambodia</a></div>\n<p>The level of <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corruption</a> in Cambodia exceeds most countries in the world. Despite adopting an \'Anti-Corruption Law\' in 2010, corruption prevails throughout the country. Corruption affects the judiciary, the police and other state institutions. Favouritism by government officials and impunity is commonplace. Lack of a clear distinction between the courts and the executive branch of government also makes for a deep politicisation of the judicial system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-globalwitness.org_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-globalwitness.org-117">[117]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Examples of areas where Cambodians encounter corrupt practices in their everyday lives include obtaining medical services, dealing with alleged traffic violations, and pursuing fair court verdicts. Companies deal with extensive red tape when obtaining licenses and permits, especially construction related permits, and the demand for and supply of bribes are commonplace in this process. The 2010 Anti-Corruption Law provided no protection to whistle-blowers, and whistle-blowers can be jailed for up to 6 months if they report corruption that cannot be proven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-globalwitness.org_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-globalwitness.org-117">[117]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Cambodia" title="Foreign relations of Cambodia">Foreign relations of Cambodia</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_President,_Smt._Pratibha_Devisingh_Patil_meeting_the_King_of_Cambodia,_HM_Preah_Bat_Samdech_Preah_Boromneath_Norodom_Sihamoni,_at_Thrown_Hall,_in_Royal_Palace_at_Phnom_Penh,_Cambodia_on_September_14,_2010.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2100" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/The_President%2C_Smt._Pratibha_Devisingh_Patil_meeting_the_King_of_Cambodia%2C_HM_Preah_Bat_Samdech_Preah_Boromneath_Norodom_Sihamoni%2C_at_Thrown_Hall%2C_in_Royal_Palace_at_Phnom_Penh%2C_Cambodia_on_September_14%2C_2010.jpg/200px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/The_President%2C_Smt._Pratibha_Devisingh_Patil_meeting_the_King_of_Cambodia%2C_HM_Preah_Bat_Samdech_Preah_Boromneath_Norodom_Sihamoni%2C_at_Thrown_Hall%2C_in_Royal_Palace_at_Phnom_Penh%2C_Cambodia_on_September_14%2C_2010.jpg/300px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/The_President%2C_Smt._Pratibha_Devisingh_Patil_meeting_the_King_of_Cambodia%2C_HM_Preah_Bat_Samdech_Preah_Boromneath_Norodom_Sihamoni%2C_at_Thrown_Hall%2C_in_Royal_Palace_at_Phnom_Penh%2C_Cambodia_on_September_14%2C_2010.jpg/400px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">King Norodom Sihamoni hosting Indian President <a href="/wiki/Pratibha_Patil" title="Pratibha Patil">Pratibha Patil</a> in 2010.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:John_Kerry_meets_with_Cambodian_Prime_Minister_Hun_Sen.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3012" data-file-width="4519" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/John_Kerry_meets_with_Cambodian_Prime_Minister_Hun_Sen.jpg/200px-John_Kerry_meets_with_Cambodian_Prime_Minister_Hun_Sen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/John_Kerry_meets_with_Cambodian_Prime_Minister_Hun_Sen.jpg/300px-John_Kerry_meets_with_Cambodian_Prime_Minister_Hun_Sen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/John_Kerry_meets_with_Cambodian_Prime_Minister_Hun_Sen.jpg/400px-John_Kerry_meets_with_Cambodian_Prime_Minister_Hun_Sen.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Hun_Sen" title="Hun Sen">Hun Sen</a> shakes hands with <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">US Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Kerry" title="John Kerry">John Kerry</a> during his visit to Cambodia on 25 January 2016.</div></div></div></div>\n<p>The foreign relations of Cambodia are handled by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_and_International_Cooperation_(Cambodia)" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs and International Cooperation (Cambodia)">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a> under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prak_Sokhon" title="Prak Sokhon">Prak Sokhon</a>. Cambodia is a member of the United Nations, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>. It is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> (ADB), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ASEAN" title="ASEAN">ASEAN</a>, and joined the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WTO" title="WTO">WTO</a> in 2004. In 2005 Cambodia attended the inaugural <a href="/wiki/East_Asia_Summit" title="East Asia Summit">East Asia Summit</a> in Malaysia.\n</p><p>Cambodia has established <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diplomatic_relations" title="Diplomatic relations">diplomatic relations</a> with numerous countries; the government reports twenty embassies in the country<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> including many of its Asian neighbours and those of important players during the Paris peace negotiations, including the US, Australia, Canada, China, the European Union (EU), Japan, and Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> As a result of its international relations, various charitable organisations have assisted with social, economic, and <a href="/wiki/Civil_engineering" title="Civil engineering">civil</a> infrastructure needs.\n</p><p>While the violent ruptures of the 1970s and 1980s have passed, several <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Border_dispute" title="Border dispute">border disputes</a> between Cambodia and its neighbours persist. There are disagreements over some offshore islands and sections of the boundary with Vietnam and undefined <a href="/wiki/Maritime_boundary" title="Maritime boundary">maritime boundaries</a>. Cambodia and Thailand also have border disputes, with troops <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cambodian-Thai_border_dispute" title="Cambodian-Thai border dispute">clashing over land</a> immediately adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Preah_Vihear_Temple" title="Preah Vihear Temple">Preah Vihear</a> temple in particular, leading to a deterioration in relations. Most of the territory belongs to Cambodia, but a combination of Thailand disrespecting international law, Thai troop upbuild in the area and lack of resources for the Cambodian military have left the situation unsettled since 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cambodia and China have cultivated ties in the 2010s. A Chinese company with the support of the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People\'s Liberation Army">People\'s Liberation Army</a> built a deep-water seaport along 90&#160;km (56&#160;mi) stretch of Cambodian coastline of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Thailand" title="Gulf of Thailand">Gulf of Thailand</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Koh_Kong_province" title="Koh Kong province">Koh Kong province</a>; the port is sufficiently deep to be used by cruise ships, <a href="/wiki/Bulk_carrier" title="Bulk carrier">bulk carriers</a> or warships. Cambodia\'s diplomatic support has been invaluable to Beijing\'s <a href="/wiki/Territorial_disputes_in_the_South_China_Sea" title="Territorial disputes in the South China Sea">effort to claim disputed areas</a> in the <a href="/wiki/South_China_Sea" title="South China Sea">South China Sea</a>. Because Cambodia is a member of ASEAN, and because under ASEAN rules "the objections of one member can thwart any group initiative", Cambodia is diplomatically useful to China as a counterweight to southeast Asian nations that have closer ties to the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Royal_Cambodian_Armed_Forces" title="Royal Cambodian Armed Forces">Royal Cambodian Armed Forces</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Cambodian_Army_soldiers,_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="960" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Royal_Cambodian_Army_soldiers%2C_2014.jpg/220px-Royal_Cambodian_Army_soldiers%2C_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Royal_Cambodian_Army_soldiers%2C_2014.jpg/330px-Royal_Cambodian_Army_soldiers%2C_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Royal_Cambodian_Army_soldiers%2C_2014.jpg/440px-Royal_Cambodian_Army_soldiers%2C_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Cambodian_Army_soldiers,_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Royal Cambodian Army officers marching</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Cambodian_Army" title="Royal Cambodian Army">Royal Cambodian Army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Cambodian_Navy" title="Royal Cambodian Navy">Royal Cambodian Navy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Cambodian_Air_Force" title="Royal Cambodian Air Force">Royal Cambodian Air Force</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Gendarmerie_of_Cambodia" title="Royal Gendarmerie of Cambodia">Royal Gendarmerie</a> collectively form the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_Cambodia" title="Military of Cambodia">Royal Cambodian Armed Forces</a>, under the command of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_National_Defence_(Cambodia)" title="Ministry of National Defence (Cambodia)">Ministry of National Defence</a>, presided over by the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Cambodia" title="Prime Minister of Cambodia">Prime Minister of Cambodia</a>. His Majesty King Norodom Sihamoni is the Supreme Commander of the Royal Cambodian Armed Forces (RCAF), and the country\'s Prime Minister Hun Sen effectively holds the position of <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a>.\n</p><p>The introduction of a revised command structure early in 2000 was a key prelude to the reorganisation of the Cambodian military. This saw the defence ministry form three subordinate general departments responsible for logistics and finance, materials and technical services, and defence services under the High Command Headquarters (HCHQ).\n</p><p>The minister of National Defense is General <a href="/wiki/Tea_Banh" title="Tea Banh">Tea Banh</a>. Banh has served as defence minister since 1979. The Secretaries of State for Defense are <a href="/wiki/Chay_Saing_Yun" title="Chay Saing Yun">Chay Saing Yun</a> and Por Bun Sreu.\n</p><p>In 2010, the Royal Cambodian Armed Forces comprised about 102,000 active personnel (200,000 reserve). Total Cambodian military spending stands at 3% of national GDP. The Royal Gendarmerie of Cambodia total more than 7,000 personnel. Its civil duties include providing security and public peace, to investigate and prevent organised crime, terrorism and other violent groups; to protect state and private property; to help and assist civilians and other emergency forces in a case of emergency, natural disaster, civil unrest and armed conflicts.\n</p><p>Hun Sen has accumulated highly centralised power in Cambodia, including a <i>praetorian guard</i> that \'appears to rival the capabilities of the country\'s regular military units\', and is allegedly used by Hun Sen to quell political opposition.\'<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_profession">Legal profession</span></h3>\n<p>The Cambodian legal profession was established in 1932. By 1978, due to the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a> regime, the entire legal system was eradicated. Judges and lawyers were executed after being deemed "class enemies" and only 6&#8211;12 legal professionals actually survived and remained in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Lawyers did not reappear until 1995 when the Bar Association of the Kingdom of Cambodia [&#6018;&#6030;&#6088;&#6040;&#6081;&#6034;&#6070;&#6044;&#6072;&#6035;&#6083;&#6038;&#6098;&#6042;&#6087;&#6042;&#6070;&#6023;&#6070;&#6030;&#6070;&#6021;&#6016;&#6098;&#6042;&#6016;&#6040;&#6098;&#6038;&#6075;&#6023;&#6070;] was created.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Cambodia" title="Human rights in Cambodia">Human rights in Cambodia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kem_Sokha_with_Sam_Rainsy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Kem_Sokha_with_Sam_Rainsy.jpg/220px-Kem_Sokha_with_Sam_Rainsy.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Kem_Sokha_with_Sam_Rainsy.jpg/330px-Kem_Sokha_with_Sam_Rainsy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Kem_Sokha_with_Sam_Rainsy.jpg/440px-Kem_Sokha_with_Sam_Rainsy.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kem_Sokha_with_Sam_Rainsy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cambodia\'s deputy opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Kem_Sokha" title="Kem Sokha">Kem Sokha</a> (left) has been arrested in September 2017 while opposition leader <a href="/wiki/Sam_Rainsy" title="Sam Rainsy">Sam Rainsy</a> (right) has lived in exile since November 2015</div></div></div>\n<p>A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_State_Department" title="US State Department">US State Department</a> report says "forces under Hun Sen and the <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_People%27s_Party" title="Cambodian People\'s Party">Cambodian People\'s Party</a> have committed frequent and large-scale abuses, including extrajudicial killings and torture, with impunity".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> According to the 2016 Global Slavery Index, an estimated 256,800 people are enslaved in modern-day Cambodia, or 1.65% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Forced land evictions by senior officials, security forces, and government-connected business leaders are commonplace in Cambodia. Land has been confiscated from hundreds of thousands of Cambodians over more than a decade for the purpose of self-enrichment and maintaining power of various groups of special interests. Credible non-governmental organisations estimate that "770,000 people have been adversely affected by land grabbing covering at least four million hectares (nearly 10 million acres) of land that have been confiscated", says Paris-based <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_for_Human_Rights" title="International Federation for Human Rights">International Federation for Human Rights</a> (FIDH).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rfa.org_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-rfa.org-129">[129]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Cambodia" title="Administrative divisions of Cambodia">Administrative divisions of Cambodia</a></div>\n<p>The autonomous municipality (<i>reach thani</i>) and provinces (<i>khaet</i>) of Cambodia are first-level administrative divisions. Cambodia is divided into 25 <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Cambodia" title="Provinces of Cambodia">provinces</a> including the autonomous municipality.\n</p><p>Municipalities and districts are the second-level administrative divisions of Cambodia. The provinces are subdivided into 159 districts and 26 municipalities. The districts and municipalities in turn are further divided into communes (<i>khum</i>) and quarters (<i>sangkat</i>).\n</p>\n<table cellspacing="2" style="text-align:right">754,000\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td>\n<th><center><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Provincial_Boundaries_in_Cambodia.svg"><img alt="Provincial Boundaries in Cambodia.svg" data-file-height="524" data-file-width="691" decoding="async" height="524" width="691"/></a>\n</center></th></tr></tbody></table>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Cambodia" title="Economy of Cambodia">Economy of Cambodia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cambodia,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="264" data-file-width="442" decoding="async" height="209" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Cambodia%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png/350px-Cambodia%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/95/Cambodia%2C_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png 1.5x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cambodia,_Trends_in_the_Human_Development_Index_1970-2010.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Cambodian position on the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, 1970&#8211;2010</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2017 Cambodia\'s per capita income is $4,022 in PPP and $1,309 in nominal per capita. Cambodia graduated from the status of a Least Developed Country to a Lower Middle Income country in the same year 2016. Most rural households depend on agriculture and its related sub-sectors. <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">Rice</a>, fish, timber, garments and rubber are Cambodia\'s major exports. The <a href="/wiki/International_Rice_Research_Institute" title="International Rice Research Institute">International Rice Research Institute</a> (IRRI) reintroduced more than 750 traditional rice varieties to Cambodia from its rice seed bank in the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> These varieties had been collected in the 1960s.\n</p><p>Based on the Economist, IMF: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annual_average_GDP_growth" title="Annual average GDP growth">Annual average GDP growth</a> for the period 2001&#8211;2010 was 7.7% making it one of the world\'s top ten countries with the highest annual average GDP growth. Tourism was Cambodia\'s fastest growing industry, with arrivals increasing from 219,000 in 1997 to over 2 million in 2007. In 2004, inflation was at 1.7% and exports at $1.6&#160;billion US$.\n</p><p>In the Cambodia country assessment "Where Have All The Poor Gone? Cambodia Poverty Assessment 2013", the World Bank concludes: "Over the seven years from 2004 through 2011, Cambodian economic growth was tremendous, ranking amid the best in the world. Moreover, household consumption increased by nearly 40 percent. And this growth was pro-poor&#8212;not only reducing inequality, but also proportionally boosting poor people\'s consumption further and faster than that of the non-poor. As a result, the poverty rate dropped from 52.2 to 20.5 percent, surpassing all expectations and far exceeding the country\'s Millennium Development Goals (MDGs) poverty target. However, the majority of these people escaped poverty only slightly: they remain highly vulnerable&#8212;even to small shocks&#8212;which could quickly bring them back into poverty."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup>\n</p><p>"Two decades of economic growth have helped make Cambodia a global leader in reducing poverty. The success story means the Southeast Asian nation that overcame a vicious civil war now is classified as a lower-middle income economy by the World Bank Group (WBG). Among 69 countries that have comparable data, Cambodia ranked fourth in terms of the fastest poverty reduction in the world from 2004&#8211;2008. (See more details of Cambodia\'s achievements on poverty reduction. The poverty rate fell to 10 percent in 2013, and further reduction of poverty is expected for both urban and rural households throughout 2015&#8211;2016.  However, human development, particularly in the areas of health and education, remains an important challenge and development priority for Cambodia"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Oil and natural gas deposits found beneath Cambodia\'s territorial waters in 2005 yield great potential but remain mostly untapped, due in part to territorial disputes with <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cambodia%27s_rice_fields.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2916" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Cambodia%27s_rice_fields.jpg/220px-Cambodia%27s_rice_fields.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Cambodia%27s_rice_fields.jpg/330px-Cambodia%27s_rice_fields.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Cambodia%27s_rice_fields.jpg/440px-Cambodia%27s_rice_fields.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cambodia%27s_rice_fields.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Paddy_field" title="Paddy field">Paddy field</a> in <a href="/wiki/Siem_Reap_Province" title="Siem Reap Province">Siem Reap</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The National Bank of Cambodia is the central bank of the kingdom and provides regulatory oversight to the country\'s banking sector and is responsible in part for increasing the foreign direct investment in the country. Between 2010 and 2012 the number of regulated banks and micro-finance institutions increased from 31 covered entities to over 70 individual institutions underlining the growth within the Cambodian banking and finance sector.\n</p><p>In 2012, Credit Bureau Cambodia was established with direct regulatory oversight by the National Bank of Cambodia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> The Credit Bureau further increases the transparency and stability within the Cambodian Banking Sector as all banks and microfinance companies are now required by law to report accurate facts and figures relating to loan performance in the country.\n</p><p>One of the largest challenges facing Cambodia is still the fact that the older population often lacks education, particularly in the countryside, which suffers from a lack of basic infrastructure. Fear of renewed political instability and corruption within the government discourage foreign investment and delay foreign aid, although there has been significant aid from bilateral and multilateral donors. Donors pledged $504&#160;million to the country in 2004,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIACB_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-CIACB-1">[1]</a></sup> while the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> alone has provided $850&#160;million in loans, grants, and technical assistance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ADB_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-ADB-136">[136]</a></sup> Bribes are often demanded from companies operating in Cambodia when obtaining licences and permits, such as construction-related permits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Battambang_Provinz_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="435" data-file-width="700" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Battambang_Provinz_01.jpg/220px-Battambang_Provinz_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Battambang_Provinz_01.jpg/330px-Battambang_Provinz_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Battambang_Provinz_01.jpg/440px-Battambang_Provinz_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Battambang_Provinz_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Farmers harvesting rice in <a href="/wiki/Battambang_Province" title="Battambang Province">Battambang Province</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Cambodia ranked among the worst places in the world for organised labour in the 2015 <a href="/wiki/International_Trade_Union_Confederation" title="International Trade Union Confederation">International Trade Union Confederation</a> (ITUC) Global Rights Index, landing in the category of countries with "no guarantee of rights".\'<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2016 Cambodia\'s National Assembly has adopted a Law on Trade Unions. "The law was proposed at a time when workers have been staging sustained protests in factories and in the streets demanding wage increases and improvements in their working conditions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> The concerns about Cambodia\'s new law are shared not only by labour and rights groups, but international organisations more generally. The <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">International Labour Organization</a> Country Office for Thailand, Cambodia and Lao PDR, has noted that the law has "several key concerns and gaps".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Independent unions and employers remain as divided as ever. "How can a factory with 25 unions survive?" asked Van Sou Ieng, chairman of the Garment Manufacturers Association in Cambodia (GMAC), adding that it was incomprehensible to expect an employer to negotiate a dispute with 25 different union leaders. A law was necessary to rein in the country\'s unions, Van Sou Ieng said. According to GMAC, last year there were 3,166 unions for the more than 500,000 workers employed in the country\'s 557 garment and textile exporting factories, and 58 footwear factories. Though garment production is already Cambodia\'s largest industry, which accounts for 26.2 percent of the country\'s Gross Domestic Product, Van Sou Ieng said without the trade union law, foreign investors will not come to do business".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup>\n</p><p>"Only with the trade union law will we, employers, be able to survive.... not only Cambodia, every country has trade union law. Those who criticize [the law] should do businesses, and [then] they will understand."\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Textiles">Textiles</span></h3>\n<p>The garment industry represents the largest portion of Cambodia\'s manufacturing sector, accounting for 80% of the country\'s exports. In 2012, the exports grew to $4.61 billion up 8% over 2011. In the first half of 2013, the garment industry reported exports worth $1.56 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-investvine_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-investvine-142">[142]</a></sup> The sector employs 335,400 workers, of which 91% are female.\n</p><p>Better Factories Cambodia was created in 2001 as a unique partnership between the UN\'s International Labour Organization (ILO) and the International Finance Corporation (IFC), a member of the World Bank Group. The programme engages with workers, employers and governments to improve working conditions and boost competitiveness of the garment industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> On May 18, 2018, the Project Advisory Committee (PAC) of the ILO Better Factories Cambodia Programme met in Phnom Penh to provide input into the draft conclusions and recommendations of the BFC\'s independent mid-term evaluation, as well as to discuss options on how to further strengthen the programme\'s transparent reporting initiative.\n</p><p>The members of the PAC concurred with the findings of the evaluation related to the impact the programme has had on the Cambodian garment sector and workers, including:\na. contributing to sustained overall growth of the garment industry\nb. improving the lives of at least half a million Cambodian workers of factories in the BFC\nprogramme and many more of their family members;\nc. ensuring that workers receive correct wages and social protection benefits\nd. virtually eliminating child labour in the sector\ne. making Cambodia\'s garment factories safer overall\nf. creating a "level playing field" for labour across garment sector\ng. influencing business practices through (1) using factory data to highlight areas for\nimprovement and (2) being a core part of risk management strategies of international\nbrands/buyers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Cambodia" title="Tourism in Cambodia">Tourism in Cambodia</a></div>\n<p>The tourism industry is the country\'s second-greatest source of <a href="/wiki/Hard_currency" title="Hard currency">hard currency</a> after the textile industry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USDOS3_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-USDOS3-74">[74]</a></sup> Between January and December 2007, visitor arrivals were 2.0 million, an increase of 18.5% over the same period in 2006. Most visitors (51%) arrived through <a href="/wiki/Siem_Reap" title="Siem Reap">Siem Reap</a> with the remainder (49%) through Phnom Penh and other destinations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CAGOV_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-CAGOV-145">[145]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other tourist destinations include <a href="/wiki/Sihanoukville_(city)" title="Sihanoukville (city)">Sihanoukville</a> in the south west which has several popular beaches and the sleepy riverside town of <a href="/wiki/Battambang" title="Battambang">Battambang</a> in the north west, both of which are a popular stop for backpackers who make up a large of portion of visitors to Cambodia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> The area around <a href="/wiki/Kampot_(city)" title="Kampot (city)">Kampot</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kep,_Cambodia" title="Kep, Cambodia">Kep</a> including the <a href="/wiki/Bokor_Hill_Station" title="Bokor Hill Station">Bokor Hill Station</a> are also of interest to visitors. Tourism has increased steadily each year in the relatively stable period since the 1993 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNTAC" title="UNTAC">UNTAC</a> elections; in 1993 there were 118,183 international tourists, and in 2009 there were 2,161,577 international tourists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most of the tourists were Japanese, Chinese, Filipinos, Americans, South Koreans and French, said the report, adding that the industry earned some 1.4 billion US dollars in 2007, accounting for almost ten percent of the kingdom\'s gross national product. Chinese-language newspaper Jianhua Daily quoted industry officials as saying that Cambodia will have three million foreign tourist arrivals in 2010 and five million in 2015. Tourism has been one of Cambodia\'s triple pillar industries. The Angkor Wat historical park in <a href="/wiki/Siem_Reap" title="Siem Reap">Siem Reap</a> province, the beaches in Sihanoukville and the capital city Phnom Penh are the main attractions for foreign tourists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cambodia\'s reputation as a safe destination for tourism however has been hindered by civil and political unrest <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> and multiple high-profile examples of serious crime perpetrated against tourists visiting the Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cambodia\'s tourist souvenir industry employs a lot of people around the main places of interest. Obviously, the quantity of souvenirs that are produced is not sufficient to face the increasing number of tourists and a majority of products sold to the tourists on the markets are imported from China, Thailand and Vietnam.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> Some of the locally produced souvenirs include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Krama (traditional scarf)</li>\n<li>Ceramic works</li>\n<li>Soap, candle, spices<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Wood carving, lacquerware, silverplating<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Painted bottles containing infused rice wine</li></ul>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:auto; max-width:608px;">\n<div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Buddhist_monks_in_front_of_the_Angkor_Wat.jpg" title="View of Angkor Wat in Siem Reap. Today Angkor Wat is Cambodia\'s main tourist attraction and is visited by many tourists from around the world."><img alt="" data-file-height="1967" data-file-width="3496" decoding="async" height="338" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Buddhist_monks_in_front_of_the_Angkor_Wat.jpg/600px-Buddhist_monks_in_front_of_the_Angkor_Wat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Buddhist_monks_in_front_of_the_Angkor_Wat.jpg/900px-Buddhist_monks_in_front_of_the_Angkor_Wat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Buddhist_monks_in_front_of_the_Angkor_Wat.jpg/1200px-Buddhist_monks_in_front_of_the_Angkor_Wat.jpg 2x" width="600"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Buddhist_monks_in_front_of_the_Angkor_Wat.jpg" title="File:Buddhist monks in front of the Angkor Wat.jpg"> </a></div><center>View of <a href="/wiki/Angkor_Wat" title="Angkor Wat">Angkor Wat</a> in <a href="/wiki/Siem_Reap_Province" title="Siem Reap Province">Siem Reap</a>. Today Angkor Wat is Cambodia\'s main tourist attraction and is visited by many tourists from around the world.</center></div>\n</div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Cambodia" title="Agriculture in Cambodia">Agriculture in Cambodia</a></div>\n<p>Agriculture is the traditional mainstay of the Cambodian economy. Agriculture accounted for 90 percent of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GDP" title="GDP">GDP</a> in 1985 and employed approximately 80 percent of the work force. <a href="/wiki/Rice" title="Rice">Rice</a> is the principal commodity. Major secondary crops include <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sweet_potatoes" title="Sweet potatoes">sweet potatoes</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bambara_groundnut" title="Bambara groundnut">groundnuts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soybean" title="Soybean">soybeans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sesame_seed" title="Sesame seed">sesame seeds</a>, dry beans, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rubber" title="Rubber">rubber</a>. The principal commercial crop is rubber. In the 1980s it was an important primary commodity, second only to rice, and one of the country\'s few sources of foreign exchange.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Cambodia" title="Transport in Cambodia">Transport in Cambodia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Road_4_to_Sihanouk.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="986" data-file-width="1562" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Road_4_to_Sihanouk.JPG/220px-Road_4_to_Sihanouk.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Road_4_to_Sihanouk.JPG/330px-Road_4_to_Sihanouk.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Road_4_to_Sihanouk.JPG/440px-Road_4_to_Sihanouk.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Road_4_to_Sihanouk.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>National Highway 4</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nek_Leoung_bridge.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="875" data-file-width="1147" decoding="async" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Nek_Leoung_bridge.jpg/220px-Nek_Leoung_bridge.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Nek_Leoung_bridge.jpg/330px-Nek_Leoung_bridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Nek_Leoung_bridge.jpg/440px-Nek_Leoung_bridge.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nek_Leoung_bridge.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Neak_Loeung_Bridge" title="Neak Loeung Bridge">Neak Loeung Bridge</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The civil war and neglect severely damaged Cambodia\'s transport system. With assistance from other countries Cambodia has been upgrading the main highways to international standards and most are vastly improved from 2006. Most main roads are now paved.\n</p><p>Cambodia has two rail lines, totalling about 612 kilometres (380 miles) of single, one-metre (3-foot-3-inch) gauge track.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CamRail_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-CamRail-158">[158]</a></sup> The lines run from the capital to Sihanoukville on the southern coast. Trains are again running to and from the Cambodian capital and popular destinations in the south. After 14 years, regular rail services between the two cities restarted recently&#160;&#8211; offering a safer option than road for travellers aiming for some beach time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> Trains also run from Phnom Penh to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sisophon" title="Sisophon">Sisophon</a> (although trains often run only as far as <a href="/wiki/Battambang" title="Battambang">Battambang</a>). As of 1987, only one passenger train per week operated between Phnom Penh and Battambang but a $141 million project, funded mostly by the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a>, has been started to revitalise the languishing rail system that will "(interlink) Cambodia with major industrial and logistics centers in Bangkok and Ho Chi Minh City".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CamRail_158-1"><a href="#cite_note-CamRail-158">[158]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Besides the main interprovincial traffic artery connecting Phnom Penh with Sihanoukville, resurfacing a former dirt road with concrete / asphalt and implementation of 5 major river crossings by means of bridges have now permanently connected Phnom Penh with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Koh_Kong_(city)" title="Koh Kong (city)">Koh Kong</a>, and hence there is now uninterrupted road access to neighbouring Thailand and their vast road system.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Siem_reap_airport.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Siem_reap_airport.JPG/220px-Siem_reap_airport.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Siem_reap_airport.JPG/330px-Siem_reap_airport.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Siem_reap_airport.JPG/440px-Siem_reap_airport.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Siem_reap_airport.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angkor_International_Airport" title="Angkor International Airport">Siem Reap International Airport</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Cambodia\'s road traffic accident rate is high by world standards. In 2004, the number of road fatalities per 10,000 vehicles was ten times higher in Cambodia than in the developed world, and the number of road deaths had doubled in the preceding three years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cambodia\'s extensive inland waterways were important historically in international trade. The <a href="/wiki/Mekong" title="Mekong">Mekong</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tonle_Sap" title="Tonle Sap">Tonle Sap</a> River, their numerous tributaries, and the Tonle Sap provided avenues of considerable length, including 3,700 kilometres (2,300 miles) navigable all year by craft drawing 0.6 metres (2.0 feet) and another 282 kilometres (175 miles) navigable to craft drawing 1.8 metres (5.9 feet).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNTRYDTA_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNTRYDTA-161">[161]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cambodia has two major ports, Phnom Penh and Sihanoukville, and five minor ones. Phnom Penh, located at the junction of the <a href="/wiki/Bassac_River" title="Bassac River">Bassac</a>, the Mekong, and the Tonle Sap rivers, is the only <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/River_port" title="River port">river port</a> capable of receiving 8,000-<a href="/wiki/Ton" title="Ton">ton</a> ships during the wet season and 5,000-ton ships during the dry season.\nWith increasing economic activity has come an increase in automobile use, though motorcycles still predominate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> "Cyclo" (as hand-me-down French) or <a href="/wiki/Cycle_rickshaw" title="Cycle rickshaw">Cycle rickshaws</a> were popular in 1990s but are increasingly replaced by remorques (carriages attached to motorcycles) and rickshaws imported from India. Cyclos are unique to Cambodia in that the cyclist is situated behind the passenger(s) seat,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> as opposed to Cycle rickshaws in neighbouring countries where the cyclist is at the front and "pulls" the carriage.\n</p><p>Cambodia has three commercial airports. <a href="/wiki/Phnom_Penh_International_Airport" title="Phnom Penh International Airport">Phnom Penh International Airport (Pochentong)</a> in Phnom Penh is the second largest in Cambodia. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angkor_International_Airport" title="Angkor International Airport">Siem Reap-Angkor International Airport</a> is the largest and serves the most international flights in and out of Cambodia. The other airport is in <a href="/wiki/Sihanoukville_(city)" title="Sihanoukville (city)">Sihanoukville</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Cambodia" title="Demographics of Cambodia">Demographics of Cambodia</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="4" style="text-align:center; background:#cfb;">Population in Cambodia<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-164">[164]</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Year\n</th>\n<th style="background:#cfb;">Million\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">1950</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">4.4\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2000</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">12.1\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:left;">2016</td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">15.8\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>As of  2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cambodia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Cambodia has an estimated population of 15,762,370 people. Cambodia\'s birth rate is 25.4 per 1,000. Its <a href="/wiki/Population_growth" title="Population growth">population growth</a> rate is 1.7%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Birth_Rate_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-Birth_Rate-165">[165]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Fifty percent of the Cambodian population is younger than 22 years old. At a 1.04 female to male ratio, Cambodia has the most female-biased sex ratio in the Greater Mekong Subregion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> Among the Cambodian population aged over 65, the female to male ratio is 1.6:1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIACB_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-CIACB-1">[1]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The total fertility rate in Cambodia was 3.0 children per woman in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDHS_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-CDHS-167">[167]</a></sup> The fertility rate was 4.0 children in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDHS_167-1"><a href="#cite_note-CDHS-167">[167]</a></sup> Women in urban areas have 2.2 children on average, compared with 3.3 children per woman in rural areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDHS_167-2"><a href="#cite_note-CDHS-167">[167]</a></sup> Fertility is highest in <a href="/wiki/Mondulkiri_Province" title="Mondulkiri Province">Mondol Kiri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ratanakiri_Province" title="Ratanakiri Province">Rattanak Kiri</a> Provinces, where women have an average of 4.5 children, and lowest in Phnom Penh where women have an average of 2.0 children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CDHS_167-3"><a href="#cite_note-CDHS-167">[167]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Cambodia" title="Ethnic groups in Cambodia">Ethnic groups in Cambodia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cambodia_ethnic_map.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1418" data-file-width="1345" decoding="async" height="464" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Cambodia_ethnic_map.svg/440px-Cambodia_ethnic_map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Cambodia_ethnic_map.svg/660px-Cambodia_ethnic_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Cambodia_ethnic_map.svg/880px-Cambodia_ethnic_map.svg.png 2x" width="440"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cambodia_ethnic_map.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An ethnic map of Cambodia</div></div></div>\n<p>The vast majority of Cambodia\'s population is of ethnic <a href="/wiki/Khmer_people" title="Khmer people">Khmer</a> origin (over 95%) who are speakers of the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_language" title="Khmer language">Khmer language</a>, the country\'s sole official language. Cambodia\'s population is largely homogeneous. Its minority groups include <a href="/wiki/Chams" title="Chams">Chams</a> (1.2%), <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_people" title="Vietnamese people">Vietnamese</a> (0.1%) and <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Cambodian" title="Chinese Cambodian">Chinese</a> (0.1%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIACB_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-CIACB-1">[1]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The largest ethnic group in Cambodia are the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_people" title="Khmer people">Khmers</a>, who comprise around 90% of the total population in Cambodia, and are indigenous to the lowland Mekong subregion in which they inhabit. The Khmers historically have lived near the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mekong_River" title="Mekong River">lower Mekong River</a> in a contiguous diagonal arc, from where modern-day Thailand, Laos and Cambodia meet in the northwest, all the way to the mouth of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mekong_River" title="Mekong River">Mekong River</a> in southeastern Vietnam.\n</p><p>The Vietnamese are the second largest ethnic minority in Cambodia, with an estimated 16,000 living in provinces concentrated in the southeast of the country adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Mekong_Delta" title="Mekong Delta">Mekong Delta</a>. Although the Vietnamese language has been determined to be a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mon%E2%80%93Khmer" title="Mon&#8211;Khmer">Mon&#8211;Khmer</a> language, there are very few cultural connections between the two peoples because the early Khmers were influenced by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_cultural_sphere" title="Indian cultural sphere">Indian cultural sphere</a> while the Vietnamese are part of the <a href="/wiki/Adoption_of_Chinese_literary_culture" title="Adoption of Chinese literary culture">Chinese cultural sphere</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-David_Chandler_2000_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-David_Chandler_2000-168">[168]</a></sup> Due to Chinese influence, Vietnamese has developed into a solidly tonal language, while Khmer has preserved the non-tonal nature of Old Austroasiatic. Ethnic tensions between the Khmer and the Vietnamese can be traced to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dark_Ages_of_Cambodia" title="Dark Ages of Cambodia">Dark Ages of Cambodia</a> (from the 16th to 19th centuries), during which time a nascent <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> each attempted to vassalise a weakened post-Angkor Cambodia, and effectively dominate all of <a href="/wiki/Indochina" title="Indochina">Indochina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-David_Chandler_2000_168-1"><a href="#cite_note-David_Chandler_2000-168">[168]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Chinese_Cambodian" title="Chinese Cambodian">Chinese Cambodians</a> are approximately 0.1% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Birth_Rate_165-1"><a href="#cite_note-Birth_Rate-165">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> Most Chinese are descended from 19th&#8211;20th-century settlers who came in search of trade and commerce opportunities during the time of the <a href="/wiki/French_Protectorate_of_Cambodia" title="French Protectorate of Cambodia">French protectorate</a>. Most are urban dwellers, engaged primarily in commerce.\n</p><p>The indigenous ethnic groups of the mountains are known collectively as Montagnards or <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Loeu" title="Khmer Loeu">Khmer Loeu</a>, a term meaning "Highland Khmer". They are descended from neolithic migrations of Mon&#8211;Khmer speakers via southern China and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austronesian" title="Austronesian">Austronesian</a> speakers from insular Southeast Asia.  Being isolated in the highlands, the various Khmer Loeu groups were not Indianized like their Khmer cousins and consequently are culturally distant from modern Khmers and often from each other, observing many pre-Indian-contact customs and beliefs.\n</p><p>The Cham are descended from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austronesian" title="Austronesian">Austronesian</a> people of <a href="/wiki/Champa" title="Champa">Champa</a>, a former kingdom on the coast of central and southern present-day Vietnam and former rival to the Khmer Empire. The Cham in Cambodia number under a million and often maintain separate villages in the southeast of the country. Almost all Cham in Cambodia are Muslims.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_centres">Population centres</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">20</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Doun_Kaev" title="Doun Kaev">Doun Kaev</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a
