id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Cambodia#Languages" title="Demographics of Cambodia">Demographics of Cambodia &#167;&#160;Languages</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Khmer_language" title="Khmer language">Khmer language</a> is a member of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mon%E2%80%93Khmer" title="Mon&#8211;Khmer">Mon&#8211;Khmer</a> subfamily of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austroasiatic_language" title="Austroasiatic language">Austroasiatic language</a> group. <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, once the language of government in <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">Indochina</a>, is still spoken by many older Cambodians, and is also the language of instruction in some schools and universities that are funded by the government of France. There is also a French-language newspaper and some TV channels are available in French. Cambodia is a member of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Francophonie" title="La Francophonie">La Francophonie</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cambodian_French_(linguistics)" title="Cambodian French (linguistics)">Cambodian French</a>, a remnant of the country\'s colonial past, is a dialect found in Cambodia and is sometimes used in government, particularly in court. However, since 1993, there has been a growing use of English, which has been replacing French as the main foreign language. English is widely taught in several universities and there is also a significant press in that language, while street signs are now bilingual in Khmer and English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> Due to this shift, English is now mostly used in Cambodia\'s international relationships and has replaced French both in Cambodia\'s stamps, since 2002, and currency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khmer_script" title="Khmer script">Khmer script</a> is derived from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Indian" title="South Indian">South Indian</a> <a href="/wiki/Pallava_script" title="Pallava script">Pallava script</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Cambodia" title="Religion in Cambodia">Religion in Cambodia</a></div>\n<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">\n<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">\n<div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:0; top:0; border-width:0 200px 200px 0; border-color:Black"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 15915.284869156px; border-left-color:Blue"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Blue"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Blue"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 3182.0515953785px; border-left-color:Red"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Red"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Red"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 1444.5585503935px; border-left-color:Green"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Green"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Green"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 506.89393637888px; border-left-color:Orange"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Orange"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Orange"></div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<p>Religion in Cambodia (2010)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pew2010_173-0"><a href="#cite_note-pew2010-173">[173]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Orange; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_Cambodia" title="Buddhism in Cambodia">Buddhism</a> (96.9%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Cambodia" title="Islam in Cambodia">Islam</a> (2.0%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Red; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Folk religion (0.6%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Blue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_Cambodia" title="Catholic Church in Cambodia">Christianity</a> (0.4%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Black; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Non religious (0.2%)</div>\n</div>\n</div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Theravada" title="Theravada">Theravada</a> <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> is the official religion of Cambodia, practised by more than 95 percent of the population with an estimated 4,392 monastery temples throughout the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> Cambodian Buddhism is deeply pervaded by <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, Tantrism, and native animism. Key concepts in Cambodian Buddhism include <a href="/wiki/Rebirth_(Buddhism)" title="Rebirth (Buddhism)">reincarnation</a>, and religious activities are focused on acquiring <i>bonn</i> (Pali <i>punna</i>, merit), and erasing <i>kamm</i> (Pali <i>kamma</i>, <a href="/wiki/Karma" title="Karma">karma</a>), which, for Khmers, means the negative results accrued from past actions.\n</p><p>Key concepts deriving from animism include the close interrelationship between spirits and the community, the efficacy of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apotropaic" title="Apotropaic">apotropaic</a> and luck-attracting actions and charms, and the possibility of manipulating one\'s life through contact with spiritual entities such as the "baromey" spirits. Hinduism has left little trace beyond the magical practices of Tantricism and a host of Hindu gods now assimilated into the spirit world (for example, the important <i>neak ta</i> spirit called <a href="/wiki/Yeay_Mao" title="Yeay Mao">Yeay Mao</a> is the modern avatar of the Hindu goddess Kali).\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahayana_Buddhism" title="Mahayana Buddhism">Mahayana Buddhism</a> is the religion of the majority of Chinese and Vietnamese in Cambodia. Elements of other religious practices, such as the veneration of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_folk_religion" title="Chinese folk religion">folk heroes</a> and ancestors, <a href="/wiki/Confucianism" title="Confucianism">Confucianism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoism</a> mix with Chinese Buddhism are also practised.\n</p><p>Islam is followed by about 2% of the population and comes in three varieties, two practised by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cham_people" title="Cham people">Cham people</a> and a third by the descendants of Malays resident in the country for generations. Cambodia\'s Muslim population is reported to be 80% ethnic Cham.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Cambodia" title="Health in Cambodia">Health in Cambodia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Defense.gov_photo_essay_120801-O-ZZ999-011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2817" data-file-width="3766" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Defense.gov_photo_essay_120801-O-ZZ999-011.jpg/220px-Defense.gov_photo_essay_120801-O-ZZ999-011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Defense.gov_photo_essay_120801-O-ZZ999-011.jpg/330px-Defense.gov_photo_essay_120801-O-ZZ999-011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Defense.gov_photo_essay_120801-O-ZZ999-011.jpg/440px-Defense.gov_photo_essay_120801-O-ZZ999-011.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Defense.gov_photo_essay_120801-O-ZZ999-011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Cambodian medical students watching a surgery operation</div></div></div>\n<p>Cambodian <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> was 72 years in 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> a major improvement since 1995 when the average life expectancy was 55.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> Health care is offered by both public and private practitioners and research has found that trust in health providers is a key factor in improving the uptake of health care services in rural Cambodia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> The government plans to increase the quality of healthcare in the country by raising awareness of <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIDS" title="AIDS">AIDS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, and other diseases.\n</p><p>Cambodia\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infant_mortality_rate" title="Infant mortality rate">infant mortality rate</a> has decreased from 115 per 1,000 live births in 1993 to 54 in 2009. In the same period, the under-five mortality rate decreased from 181 to 115 per 1,000 live births.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cambodiawho_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-cambodiawho-179">[179]</a></sup> In the province with worst health indicators, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Health_in_Ratanakiri_Province" title="Health in Ratanakiri Province">Ratanakiri</a>, 22.9% of children die before age five.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cambodia was once one of the most <a href="/wiki/Land_mines_in_Cambodia" title="Land mines in Cambodia">landmined</a> countries in the world. According to some estimates, unexploded <a href="/wiki/Land_mine" title="Land mine">land mines</a> have been responsible for over 60,000 civilian deaths and thousands more maimed or injured since 1970.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBSORG_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-PBSORG-181">[181]</a></sup> The number of reported landmine casualties has sharply decreased, from 800 in 2005 to 111 in 2013 (22 dead and 89 injured).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> Adults that survive landmines often require <a href="/wiki/Amputation" title="Amputation">amputation</a> of one or more limbs and have to resort to begging for survival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PBSORG_181-1"><a href="#cite_note-PBSORG-181">[181]</a></sup> Cambodia is expected to be free of land mines by 2020<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> but the social and economic legacy, including orphans and one in 290 people being an amputee,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> is expected to affect Cambodia for years to come.\n</p><p>"In Cambodia, landmines and exploded ordnance alone have caused 44,630 injuries between 1979 and 2013, according to the Cambodia Mine/UXO Victim Information System"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Cambodia" title="Education in Cambodia">Education in Cambodia</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education,_Youth_and_Sport_(Cambodia)" title="Ministry of Education, Youth and Sport (Cambodia)">Ministry of Education, Youth and Sports</a> is responsible for establishing national policies and guidelines for education in Cambodia. The Cambodian education system is heavily decentralised, with three levels of government, central, provincial and district &#8211; responsible for its management. The constitution of Cambodia promulgates free compulsory education for nine years, guaranteeing the universal right to basic quality education.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Institute_of_Foreign_Languages.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="682" data-file-width="1023" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Institute_of_Foreign_Languages.jpg/220px-Institute_of_Foreign_Languages.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Institute_of_Foreign_Languages.jpg/330px-Institute_of_Foreign_Languages.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Institute_of_Foreign_Languages.jpg/440px-Institute_of_Foreign_Languages.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Institute_of_Foreign_Languages.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Foreign_Languages" title="Institute of Foreign Languages">Institute of Foreign Languages</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_University_of_Phnom_Penh" title="Royal University of Phnom Penh">Royal University of Phnom Penh</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The 2008 Cambodian census estimated that 77.6% of the population was literate (85.1% of men and 70.9% of women).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CIACB_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-CIACB-1">[1]</a></sup> Male youth age (15&#8211;24 years) have a literacy rate of 89% compared to 86% for females.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The education system in Cambodia continues to face many challenges, but during the past years there have been significant improvements, especially in terms of primary net enrolment gains, the introduction of program based-budgeting, and the development of a policy framework which helps disadvantaged children to gain access to education. The country has also significantly invested in <a href="/wiki/Vocational_education" title="Vocational education">vocational education</a>, especially in rural areas, to tackle poverty and unemployment.\n<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup>  Two of Cambodia\'s most acclaimed universities are based in Phnom Penh.\n</p><p>Traditionally, education in Cambodia was offered by the wats (Buddhist temples), thus providing education exclusively for the male population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a> regime, education suffered significant setbacks. Education has also suffered setbacks from <a href="/wiki/Child_labour_in_Cambodia" title="Child labour in Cambodia">child labour</a>, A study by Kim (2011) reports that most employed children in Cambodia are enrolled in school but their employment is associated with late school entry, negative impacts on their learning outcomes, and increased drop out rates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup>\n</p><p>With respects to academic performance among Cambodian primary school children, research showed that parental attitudes and beliefs played a significant role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> Specifically, the study found that poorer academic achievement among children were associated with parents holding stronger fatalistic beliefs (i.e., human strength cannot change destiny). The study further found that "length of residence" of parents in the community in which they stay predicted better academic achievement among their children. Overall, the study pointed out to the role of social capital in educational performance and access in the Cambodian society in which family attitudes and beliefs are central to the findings.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Crime">Crime</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Crime_in_Cambodia" title="Crime in Cambodia">Crime in Cambodia</a></div>\n<p>In 2012, Cambodia had a murder rate of 6.5 per 100,000 population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNODC_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNODC-192">[192]</a></sup> On a national level, there were a total of 964 murders reported in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNODC_192-1"><a href="#cite_note-UNODC-192">[192]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_Cambodia" title="Prostitution in Cambodia">Prostitution is illegal in Cambodia</a> but yet appears to be prevalent. In a series of 1993 interviews of women about prostitution, three quarters of the interviewees found being a prostitute to be a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norm_(social)" title="Norm (social)">norm</a> and a profession they felt was not shameful having.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barry_1_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barry_1-193">[193]</a></sup> That same year, it was estimated that there were about 100,000 sex workers in Cambodia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barry_1_193-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barry_1-193">[193]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Cambodia" title="Culture of Cambodia">Culture of Cambodia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Preah_Ko_Preah_Keo" title="Preah Ko Preah Keo">Preah Ko Preah Keo</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vorvong-Sorvong-tale-Pavie9.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="556" data-file-width="331" decoding="async" height="370" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Vorvong-Sorvong-tale-Pavie9.jpg/220px-Vorvong-Sorvong-tale-Pavie9.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Vorvong-Sorvong-tale-Pavie9.jpg/330px-Vorvong-Sorvong-tale-Pavie9.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b4/Vorvong-Sorvong-tale-Pavie9.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vorvong-Sorvong-tale-Pavie9.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 19th-century illustration tale of <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_literature" title="Cambodian literature">Vorvong &amp; Sorvong</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Various factors contribute to the Cambodian culture including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Theravada_Buddhism" title="Theravada Buddhism">Theravada Buddhism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_culture" title="French culture">French colonialism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Angkor" title="Angkor">Angkorian culture</a>, and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Modern_globalisation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Modern globalisation (page does not exist)">modern globalisation</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Culture_and_Fine_Arts,_Cambodia" title="Ministry of Culture and Fine Arts, Cambodia">Cambodian Ministry of Culture and Fine Arts</a> is responsible for promoting and developing Cambodian culture. Cambodian culture not only includes the culture of the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Krom" title="Khmer Krom">lowland</a> ethnic majority, but also some 20 culturally distinct hill tribes colloquially known as the <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Loeu" title="Khmer Loeu">Khmer Loeu</a>, a term coined by <a href="/wiki/Norodom_Sihanouk" title="Norodom Sihanouk">Norodom Sihanouk</a> to encourage unity between the highlanders and lowlanders.\n</p><p>Rural Cambodians wear a <a href="/wiki/Krama" title="Krama">krama</a> scarf which is a unique aspect of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cambodian_clothing" title="Cambodian clothing">Cambodian clothing</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Sampeah" title="Sampeah">sampeah</a> is a traditional Cambodian greeting or a way of showing respect to others. Khmer culture, as developed and spread by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khmer_empire" title="Khmer empire">Khmer empire</a>, has distinctive styles of dance, architecture and sculpture, which have been exchanged with neighbouring <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> throughout history. <a href="/wiki/Angkor_Wat" title="Angkor Wat">Angkor Wat</a> (<i>Angkor</i> means "city" and <i>Wat</i> "temple") is the best preserved example of Khmer architecture from the Angkorian era along with hundreds of other temples that have been discovered in and around the region.\n</p><p>Traditionally, the Khmer people have a recorded information on <a href="/wiki/Palm-leaf_manuscript" title="Palm-leaf manuscript"><i>Tra</i> leaves</a>. <i>Tra</i> leaf books record legends of the Khmer people, the Ramayana, the origin of Buddhism and other prayer books. They are taken care of by wrapping in cloth to protect from moisture and the climate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bon_Om_Thook" title="Bon Om Thook">Bon Om Tuuk</a> (Festival of Boat Racing), the annual boat rowing contest, is the most attended Cambodian national festival. Held at the end of the rainy season when the Mekong river begins to sink back to its normal levels allowing the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tonle_Sap_River" title="Tonle Sap River">Tonle Sap River</a> to reverse flow, approximately 10% of Cambodia\'s population attends this event each year to play games, give thanks to the moon, watch fireworks, dine, and attend the boat race in a carnival-type atmosphere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KMGOV_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-KMGOV-195">[195]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Popular games include soccer, kicking a <i>sey,</i> which is similar to a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Footbag" title="Footbag">footbag</a>, and chess. Based on the classical Indian solar calendar and Theravada Buddhism, the <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_New_Year" title="Cambodian New Year">Cambodian New Year</a> is a major holiday that takes place in April. Recent artistic figures include singers <a href="/wiki/Sinn_Sisamouth" title="Sinn Sisamouth">Sinn Sisamouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ros_Serey_Sothea" title="Ros Serey Sothea">Ros Serey Sothea</a> (and later <a href="/wiki/Meng_Keo_Pichenda" title="Meng Keo Pichenda">Meng Keo Pichenda</a>), who introduced new musical styles to the country.\n</p><p>Every year, Cambodians visit <a href="/wiki/Pagoda" title="Pagoda">pagodas</a> across the country to mark the \'Festival of the Dead\' or <a href="/wiki/Pchum_Ben" title="Pchum Ben">Pchum Ben</a>. During the 15-day festival, people offer prayers and food to the spirits of their dead relatives. For most of the Cambodians, it is a time to remember their relatives, who died during 1975-1979 <a href="/wiki/Khmer_Rouge" title="Khmer Rouge">Khmer Rouge</a> regime.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Cambodia" title="Cuisine of Cambodia">Cuisine of Cambodia</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;max-width:332px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:103px;max-width:103px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:125px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Currysaraman.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="699" data-file-width="564" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Currysaraman.jpg/101px-Currysaraman.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Currysaraman.jpg/152px-Currysaraman.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Currysaraman.jpg/202px-Currysaraman.jpg 2x" width="101"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:225px;max-width:225px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:125px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Prahokktis.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="396" data-file-width="704" decoding="async" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Prahokktis.jpg/223px-Prahokktis.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Prahokktis.jpg/335px-Prahokktis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Prahokktis.jpg/446px-Prahokktis.jpg 2x" width="223"/></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:199px;max-width:199px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:147px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kampot_pepper_crab.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Kampot_pepper_crab.jpg/197px-Kampot_pepper_crab.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Kampot_pepper_crab.jpg/296px-Kampot_pepper_crab.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Kampot_pepper_crab.jpg/394px-Kampot_pepper_crab.jpg 2x" width="197"/></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:129px;max-width:129px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:147px;overflow:hidden"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Somlorkoko.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="740" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Somlorkoko.jpg/127px-Somlorkoko.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Somlorkoko.jpg/191px-Somlorkoko.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Somlorkoko.jpg/254px-Somlorkoko.jpg 2x" width="127"/></a></div></div><div style="clear:left"></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">Clockwise from top left: <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_cuisine" title="Cambodian cuisine">Samlar kari</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_cuisine" title="Cambodian cuisine">Prahok ktis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cambodian_cuisine" title="Cambodian cuisine">Kampot pepper crab</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samlar_kakou" title="Samlar kakou">Samlar kako</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Rice is the staple grain, as in other Southeast Asian countries. Fish from the Mekong and Tonle Sap rivers is also an important part of the diet. The supply of fish and fish products for food and trade as of  2000<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Cambodia&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> was 20 kilograms (44 pounds) per person or 2&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Avoirdupois" title="Avoirdupois">ounces</a> per day per person.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EARTH_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-EARTH-197">[197]</a></sup> Some of the fish can be made into <a href="/wiki/Prahok" title="Prahok">prahok</a> for longer storage.\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Cambodia" title="Cuisine of Cambodia">cuisine of Cambodia</a> contains tropical fruits, soups and noodles. Key ingredients are <a href="/wiki/Kaffir_lime" title="Kaffir lime">kaffir lime</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lemon_grass" title="Lemon grass">lemon grass</a>, garlic, <a href="/wiki/Fish_sauce" title="Fish sauce">fish sauce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soy_sauce" title="Soy sauce">soy sauce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Curry" title="Curry">curry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamarind" title="Tamarind">tamarind</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ginger" title="Ginger">ginger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oyster_sauce" title="Oyster sauce">oyster sauce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coconut_milk" title="Coconut milk">coconut milk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Black_pepper" title="Black pepper">black pepper</a>. Some delicacies are &#6035;&#6086;&#6036;&#6025;&#6098;&#6021;&#6075;&#6016; (Num Banh chok), &#6050;&#6070;&#6040;&#6089;&#6075;&#6016; (Amok), &#6050;&#6070;&#6038;&#6072;&#6020; (Ah Ping).  The country also boasts various distinct local street foods, such as <a href="/wiki/Fried_spider" title="Fried spider">fried spiders</a>.\n</p><p>French influence on Cambodian cuisine includes the Cambodian red curry with toasted <a href="/wiki/Baguette" title="Baguette">baguette</a> bread. The toasted baguette pieces are dipped in the curry and eaten. Cambodian red curry is also eaten with rice and <a href="/wiki/Rice_vermicelli" title="Rice vermicelli">rice vermicelli</a> noodles. Probably the most popular dine out dish, <a href="/wiki/Kuy_teav" title="Kuy teav">kuy teav</a>, is a <i>pork broth</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rice_noodle" title="Rice noodle">rice noodle</a> <a href="/wiki/Noodle_soup" title="Noodle soup">soup</a> with fried garlic, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scallions" title="Scallions">scallions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scallion" title="Scallion">green onions</a> that may also contain various toppings such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beef_balls" title="Beef balls">beef balls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shrimp" title="Shrimp">shrimp</a>, pork liver or lettuce. Kampot pepper is reputed to be the best in the world and accompanies crab at the Kep crab shacks and squid in the restaurants on the Ou Trojak Jet river.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup> The cuisine is relatively unknown to the world compared to that of its neighbours Thailand and Vietnam.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drinks">Drinks</span></h3>\n<p>Cambodians drink plenty of tea, grown in <a href="/wiki/Mondulkiri_Province" title="Mondulkiri Province">Mondulkiri Province</a> and around Kirirom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> <i>tai krolap</i> is a strong tea, made by putting water and a mass of tea leaves into a small glass, placing a saucer on top, and turning the whole thing upside down to brew. When it\'s dark enough, the tea is decanted into another cup and plenty of sugar added, but no milk. Lemon tea <i>tai kdao kroich chhmaa</i>, made with Chinese red-dust tea and lemon juice, is refreshing both hot and iced, and is generally served with a hefty dose of sugar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-roughguides.com_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-roughguides.com-200">[200]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Regarding coffee, the beans are generally imported from Laos and Vietnam &#8211; although domestically produced coffee from <a href="/wiki/Ratanakiri_Province" title="Ratanakiri Province">Ratanakiri Province</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mondulkiri_Province" title="Mondulkiri Province">Mondulkiri Province</a> can be found in some places. Beans are traditionally roasted with butter and sugar, plus various other ingredients that might include anything from rum to pork fat, giving the beverage a strange, sometimes faintly chocolatey aroma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-roughguides.com_200-1"><a href="#cite_note-roughguides.com-200">[200]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Cambodia has several industrial breweries, located mainly in <a href="/wiki/Sihanoukville_Province" title="Sihanoukville Province">Sihanoukville Province</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phnom_Penh" title="Phnom Penh">Phnom Penh</a>. There are also a growing number of microbreweries in <a href="/wiki/Phnom_Penh" title="Phnom Penh">Phnom Penh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siem_Reap" title="Siem Reap">Siem Reap</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Rice_wine" title="Rice wine">Rice wine</a> is a popular alcoholic drink. Its quality varies widely and it is often infused with fruits or medicinal herbs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> When prepared with macerated fruits or spices, like the <a href="/wiki/Sombai" title="Sombai">Sombai</a> liqueur, it is called <i>sraa tram</i> (or soaked wine) and has gained more and more popularity with the development of tourism as it is smoother to drink than plain rice wine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women">Women</span></h3>\n<table class="box-POV plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-POV" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Unbalanced scales.svg" data-file-height="354" data-file-width="400" decoding="async" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/45px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/68px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/90px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 2x" width="45"/></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">The <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">neutrality</a> of this section is <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NPOV_dispute" title="Wikipedia:NPOV dispute">disputed</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Relevant discussion may be found on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Cambodia##" title="Talk:Cambodia">talk page</a>. Please do not remove this message until <a href="/wiki/Template:POV#When_to_remove" title="Template:POV">conditions to do so are met</a>.</span> <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">December 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Cambodia" title="Women in Cambodia">Women in Cambodia</a></div>\n<p>Khmer women are traditionally expected to be modest, soft-spoken, well-mannered,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mekong_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mekong-207">[207]</a></sup> industrious,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Status_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-Status-208">[208]</a></sup>  act as the family\'s caregivers and caretakers<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mekong_207-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mekong-207">[207]</a></sup> and financial controllers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Status_208-1"><a href="#cite_note-Status-208">[208]</a></sup> maintain their virginity until marriage, become faithful wives,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mekong_207-2"><a href="#cite_note-Mekong-207">[207]</a></sup> and act as advisors to their husbands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Status_208-2"><a href="#cite_note-Status-208">[208]</a></sup> The "light" walking and refinement of Cambodian women is further described as being "quiet in [...] movements that one cannot hear the sound of their <a href="/wiki/Silk" title="Silk">silk</a> skirt rustling".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Status_208-3"><a href="#cite_note-Status-208">[208]</a></sup> As financial controllers, the women of Cambodia can be identified as having  household authority at the familial level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EC_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-EC-209">[209]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Cambodia" title="Sport in Cambodia">Sport in Cambodia</a></div>\n<p>Football (soccer) is one of the most popular sports, although professional organised sports are not as prevalent in Cambodia as in western countries because of the economic conditions. Soccer was brought to Cambodia by the French and became popular with the locals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cambodia_national_football_team" title="Cambodia national football team">Cambodia national football team</a> managed fourth in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_Cup_1972" title="Asian Cup 1972">1972 Asian Cup</a>, but development has slowed since the civil war.\n</p><p>Western sports such as basketball, volleyball, bodybuilding, field hockey, rugby union, golf, and baseball are gaining popularity. Volleyball is by far the most popular sport in the country. Native sports include <a href="/wiki/Dragon_boat" title="Dragon boat">traditional boat racing</a>, buffalo racing, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pradal_Serey" title="Pradal Serey">Pradal Serey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khmer_traditional_wrestling" title="Khmer traditional wrestling">Khmer traditional wrestling</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bokator" title="Bokator">Bokator</a>. Cambodia first participated in the Olympics during the <a href="/wiki/Cambodia_at_the_1956_Summer_Olympics" title="Cambodia at the 1956 Summer Olympics">1956 Summer Olympic Games</a> sending <a href="/wiki/Equestrian_at_the_Summer_Olympics" title="Equestrian at the Summer Olympics">equestrian</a> riders. Cambodia also hosted the <a href="/wiki/GANEFO" title="GANEFO">GANEFO</a> Games, the alternative to the Olympics, in the 1960s.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dance">Dance</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Dance_in_Cambodia" title="Dance in Cambodia">Dance in Cambodia</a></div>\n<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Angkor_Wat_-_050_Apsaras_(8580603733).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Angkor_Wat_-_050_Apsaras_%288580603733%29.jpg/200px-Angkor_Wat_-_050_Apsaras_%288580603733%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Angkor_Wat_-_050_Apsaras_%288580603733%29.jpg/300px-Angkor_Wat_-_050_Apsaras_%288580603733%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Angkor_Wat_-_050_Apsaras_%288580603733%29.jpg/400px-Angkor_Wat_-_050_Apsaras_%288580603733%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Apsara dancers at <a href="/wiki/Angkor_Wat" title="Angkor Wat">Angkor Wat</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Danseuses_kmer_(2).JPG"><img alt="" data-file-height="1066" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Danseuses_kmer_%282%29.JPG/200px-Danseuses_kmer_%282%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Danseuses_kmer_%282%29.JPG/300px-Danseuses_kmer_%282%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Danseuses_kmer_%282%29.JPG/400px-Danseuses_kmer_%282%29.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">Khmer <a href="/wiki/Robam_Tep_Apsara" title="Robam Tep Apsara">Apsara</a> dancers</div></div></div></div>\n<p>Cambodian dance can be divided into three main categories: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khmer_classical_dance" title="Khmer classical dance">Khmer classical dance</a>, folk dance, and social dances. The exact origins of Khmer classical dance are disputed. Most native Khmer scholars trace modern dance forms back to the time of <a href="/wiki/Angkor" title="Angkor">Angkor</a>, seeing similarities in the temple engravings of the period, while others hold that modern Khmer dance styles were learned (or re-learned) from Siamese court dancers in the 1800s.\n</p><p>Khmer classical dance is the form of stylised performance art established in the royal courts of Cambodia exhibited for both entertainment and ceremonial purposes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UnescoDance_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-UnescoDance-211">[211]</a></sup> The dances are performed by intricately costumed, highly trained men and women on public occasions for tribute, invocation or to enact traditional stories and epic poems such as <a href="/wiki/Reamker" title="Reamker">Reamker</a>, the Khmer version of the <a href="/wiki/Ramayana" title="Ramayana">Ramayana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cravath1968_212-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cravath1968-212">[212]</a></sup> Known formally as <i>Robam Preah Reach Trop</i> (<span lang="km" title="Khmer language text">&#6042;&#6036;&#6070;&#6086;&#6038;&#6098;&#6042;&#6087;&#6042;&#6070;&#6023;&#6033;&#6098;&#6042;&#6038;&#6098;&#6041;</span> "theater of royal wealth") it is set to the music of a <a href="/wiki/Pinpeat" title="Pinpeat">pinpeat</a> ensemble accompanied by a vocal chorus.\n</p><p>Cambodian folk dance, often performed to <a href="/wiki/Mahori" title="Mahori">mahori</a> music, celebrates the various cultural and ethnic groups of Cambodia. Folk dances originated in the villages and are performed, for the most part, by the villagers for the villagers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FolkDance_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-FolkDance-213">[213]</a></sup> The movements are less stylised and the clothing worn is that of the people the dancers are portraying, such as hill tribes, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cham_people_(Asia)" title="Cham people (Asia)">Chams</a> or farmers. Typically faster-paced than classical dance, folk dances display themes of the "common person" such as love, comedy or warding off evil spirits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FolkDance_213-1"><a href="#cite_note-FolkDance-213">[213]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Social dances are those performed by guests at banquets, parties or other informal social gatherings. Khmer traditional social dances are analogous to those of other Southeast Asian nations. Examples include the <a href="/wiki/Circle_dance" title="Circle dance">circle dances</a> <a href="/wiki/Romvong" title="Romvong">Romvong</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romkbach" title="Romkbach">Romkbach</a> as well as <i>Saravan</i> and <i>Lam Leav</i>. Modern western popular dances including <a href="/wiki/Cha-cha-cha_(dance)" title="Cha-cha-cha (dance)">Cha-cha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bolero" title="Bolero">Bolero</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Madison_(dance)" title="Madison (dance)">Madison</a>, have also influenced Cambodian social dance.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Cambodia" title="Music of Cambodia">Music of Cambodia</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sinn_Sisamouth.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="283" data-file-width="180" decoding="async" height="283" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/02/Sinn_Sisamouth.jpg" width="180"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sinn_Sisamouth.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sinn_Sisamouth" title="Sinn Sisamouth">Sinn Sisamouth</a>, a famous Cambodian singer</div></div></div>\n<p>Traditional Cambodian music dates back as far as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khmer_empire" title="Khmer empire">Khmer Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-umbc_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-umbc-214">[214]</a></sup> Royal dances like the <a href="/wiki/Apsara" title="Apsara">Apsara</a> Dance are icons of the Cambodian culture as are the Mahori ensembles that accompany them. More rural forms of music include <i>Chapei</i> and <i>A Yai</i>. The former is popular among the older generation and is most often a solo performance of a man plucking a Cambodian guitar (<i>chapei</i>) in between <a href="/wiki/A_cappella" title="A cappella">a cappella</a> verses. The lyrics usually have moral or religious theme.\n</p><p><i>A Yai</i> can be performed solo or by a man and woman and is often comedic in nature. It is a form of lyrical poetry, often full of double entendres, that can be either scripted or completely impromptu and <a href="/wiki/Ad_libitum" title="Ad libitum">ad-libbed</a>. When sung by a duo, the man and women take turns, "answering" the other\'s verse or posing riddles for the other to solve, with short instrumental breaks in between verses. <i>Pleng kaah</i> (lit. "wedding music") is a set of traditional music and songs played both for entertainment and as accompaniment for the various ceremonial parts of a traditional, days-long Khmer wedding.\n</p><p>Cambodian popular music is performed with western style instruments or a mixture of traditional and western instruments. Dance music is composed in particular styles for social dances. The music of crooner <a href="/wiki/Sinn_Sisamouth" title="Sinn Sisamouth">Sinn Sisamouth</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ros_Sereysothea" title="Ros Sereysothea">Ros Sereysothea</a> from the 1960s to the 1970s is considered to be the classic pop music of Cambodia. During the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khmer_rouge" title="Khmer rouge">Khmer Rouge Revolution</a>, many classic and popular singers of the 1960s and 1970s were murdered, starved to death, or overwork to death by the Khmer Rouge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup> and many original master tapes from the period were lost or destroyed.\n</p><p>In the 1980s, Keo Surath, (a refugee resettled in the United States) and others carried on the legacy of the classic singers, often remaking their popular songs. The 1980s and 1990s also saw the rise in popularity of <i><a href="/wiki/Kantrum" title="Kantrum">kantrum</a></i>, a music style of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Khmer_people" title="Northern Khmer people">Khmer Surin</a> set to modern instrumentation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[216]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Australian <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" title="Hip hop">hip hop</a> group Astronomy Class has recorded with Kak Channthy, a native born Cambodian female singer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[217]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Will_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-Will-218">[218]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Dengue_Fever_(band)" title="Dengue Fever (band)">Dengue Fever</a> rock and roll band features a Cambodian female singer and back-up band from California. It is classified as "<a href="/wiki/World_music" title="World music">world music</a>" and combines Cambodian music with Western style rock.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Science_and_technology">Science and technology</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Science_and_technology_in_Cambodia" title="Science and technology in Cambodia">Science and technology in Cambodia</a></div>\n<p>A National Committee for Science and Technology representing 11 ministries has been in place since 1999. Although seven ministries are responsible for the country\'s 33 public universities, the majority of these institutions come under the umbrella of the Ministry of Education, Youth and Support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-219">[219]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2010, the Ministry of Education, Youth and Support approved a Policy on Research Development in the Education Sector. This move represented a first step towards a national approach to research and development across the university sector and the application of research for the purposes of national development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_219-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-219">[219]</a></sup>\n</p><p>This policy was followed by the country\'s first <i>National Science and Technology Master Plan 2014&#8211;2020</i>. It was officially launched by the Ministry of Planning in December 2014, as the culmination of a two-year process supported by the <a href="/wiki/Korea_International_Cooperation_Agency" title="Korea International Cooperation Agency">Korea International Cooperation Agency</a>. The plan makes provision for establishing a science and technology foundation to promote industrial innovation, with a particular focus on agriculture, primary industry and ICTs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_219-2"><a href="#cite_note-:0-219">[219]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul
